# Translated Footnotes

[^1]: Title of the original text: "Typikon of the Ruthenian Catholic Church." "Ruthenian" is the ancient name for Ukrainians.
[^2]: Excerpt from Appendix XXXI.
[^3]: Let it be known, that the Synod provides the rule only of this, the 1st part. The rules of the other four parts are presented according to Slavic and Greek liturgical books, and also according to the customs of our churches.
[^3a]: E. g., Menaion September 9 or 11.
[^4]: Corrected by me (Ivan Dutka), since in the translation this service was omitted.
[^5]: The Rubric of the Liturgy is not given, for it is given in detail in the newly published Sluzhebnyky (lit. "Service Books").
[^6]: The Greek Euchologia and Slavonic Menaia (December 25 at the Vigil with Great Compline) prescribe also the phelonion; the rubric of our Sluzhebnyky and the Moscow Typikons prescribe only the epitrachelion. Also, the Greek Typikon mentions the phelonion for the first time at the Entrance, prescribing: Και ειςελΰοντες (priest and deacon) αλασσουσιν την ιερατικην στολην εν τω διακονικό. (Καιφ. β) /And, having entered, they dress in the sacred robes (Chapter 2)/.
[^7]: Likewise in the order of the Divine Service published by Bp. Tsikhanovsky for the use of the clergy of his Kholm Eparchy, this exclamation is prescribed for one of the deacons; in the Greek Euchologion -- to the Reader τω Αναγνώστη or Ευταξιω /the Master of Ceremonies/; in the Greek Typikon -- to the serving cleric who lights the candles Κανδηλαπτη (Sacristæ).
[^8]: The Greek Typikon prescribes this to the Priest, and this is evident, for according to its rubric, from the beginning it is not the Deacon who serves, but the Priest himself.
[^9]: The Greek Typikon orders the Deacon to mention the service from the litany "In peace let us pray to the Lord," however, the Greek Euchologia do not forbid him to serve from the beginning: Ει μη φορεση ο διάκονος εις την αρχήν του Εσπερινού, ενδύεται ψαλλομενου του γ αντίφωνου του ψαλτηρίου, ει εστίν Στιχολογια; ει δε μη, του Προοιμιακου ψαλλομενου /If the Deacon has not vested from the beginning of Vespers, let him vest during the singing of the prefatory psalm/. Our Sluzhebnyky prescribe for the Deacon to begin serving already from the beginning of Vespers, but prescribe the censing to the Priest himself; the Synod approves the current custom for two deacons to cense. Regarding what some say, that it is not proper for two deacons to serve at the Divine Services, but only one, because the rubrics mention only one, the Synod does not accept this, and rightly so. And since there is nothing against our rite when several priests serve concelebrating, even though the rubrics mention only one priest, so nothing prevents the service of several deacons.
[^10]: The Greek Typikon prescribes for the Priest, before "Glory to the Holy," to make the sign of the cross with the censer before the Holy Table three times, and the Euchologion -- to sing "Glory to the Holy" while censing the Holy Table.
[^11]: In the Greek Ευχολογ. /Euchologion/, in the order of Vespers, it is presented: Και φησιν (ο διάκονος): Ευλογησον Δέσποτα το ΰυμιαμα. Και ο Ιερεύς ευλογεί αυτό λέγων: Ευλογητος ο θεός ημών, πάντοτε /And (the Deacon) exclaims: "Bless, Master, the censer." And the Priest blesses, saying: "Blessed is our God, always"/ and at subsequent censings, the prayer "Incense we offer to Thee" is not mentioned, but only at the beginning. Therefore, it is proper to adhere to this rule at the Liturgy as well, using this prayer only once, at the beginning.
[^12]: The Greek Ευχολογιον /Euchologion/ prescribes to cense only the Holy Table.
[^13]: In some parishes, they still bend their knees and heads to the ground, as presented in the Greek Typikon, in which: Και ημών κλιναντων, και επί γης κεκυφωτων, (Καιφ. β) /And while we have bowed and bent down to the ground (Chapter 2)/.
[^14]: Since no Typikon (the Synod testifies) prescribes censing in the temple here, it would be better if the deacons cense from the place of the Litiya when they arrive there. And since this is better, we have placed such a rubric in the text, and we have completely rejected the worse existing local custom of censing the Holy Table and the local icons as at "Lord, I have cried," although the Synod mentions it too. However, if there are icons in the narthex, it is proper to cense them first, for the ancient Typikons prescribe so.
[^15]: To exclaim at this place "Bless, Master" is prescribed for the Deacon also by the Greek Διακονικον /Diakonikon/. The same is prescribed also by the Menaion at Great Compline of the Nativity of Christ and Theophany.
[^16]: The Greek Ευχολογ. /Euchologion/. Likewise the Pochaiv Triodion at Matins of Pascha Sunday.
[^17]: Some of us consider that here it is not proper to say "Lord, bless," but only "Bless," because here a blessing is not asked from the Lord, but from the Priest. But this we do not know for certain, for in other Typikons, namely in the Moscow Typikons and Horologia in the order of Vespers, and in the Greek Horologia at Daily Midnight Office, the words "Lord" are absent; however, in our Horologia (at the end of Matins) and in the Tserkovne Oko (lit. "Eye of the Church"), and in the Greek Euchologia in the order of Vespers this word is given. Here are the words of the Roman Euchologion: "Ο ιερεύς ησυχως: Δόξα σοι ο θεός, η ελπις ημών, δόξα σοι; και λεγουσιν οι Αδελφοί: Δόξα, και νυν, Κύριε ευλογησον /The Priest quietly: 'Glory to Thee, O God, our hope, glory to Thee.' And the brethren say: 'Glory, Both now,' 'Lord, bless'/." Therefore, both the former and the latter are good, for it is possible to ask the Lord God for a blessing at the conclusion of the Divine Service, just as is asked at Vespers with Vigil, at the beginning of which the Deacon, or the Priest himself, exclaims: Κύριε ευλογησον /"Lord, bless"/.
[^18]: (similar to Daily).
[^19]: All this the Greek Horologion also presents. The Peremyshl Prayer Book incorrectly does not present them; incorrectly also our Horologia begin them from the Trisagion, not prescribing "Glory to Thee, our God, glory to Thee" and "O Heavenly King."
[^20]: However, it is better presented in the Greek Horologia -- only one troparion, that is of the current Saint, or the four aforementioned: "O God of our Fathers" with the three others, without distinction of day. In the Greek Menaia the Saint does not always have a troparion and, when he does not have one, then the general troparia are taken -- "O God of our Fathers"; when he has one, then to the Saint. With us, because the current Saint in the Menaion always has a troparion, then, if it were taken always, the troparia "O God of our Fathers" would be superfluous; so that they not be superfluous, they are taken daily, and to the Saints -- only to the Polyeleos ones. The troparion of the day and of the Temple is given only in the Slavonic Typikons.
[^21]: After "Blessed is our God" there will be also "Glory to Thee, our God, glory to Thee," "O Heavenly King," Trisagion etc. up to "Come, let us worship," as the Menaion of December 25 presents.
[^22]: To the aforementioned cases which the Greek and Slavonic Typikons present, the Moscow Octoechos of 1782 adds also other Feasts of the Lord and of the Theotokos, presenting at the Midnight Office on the feast day itself, on the first day of Afterfeast, the troparion and kontakion of the feast; however, we do not have this new Typikon.
[^23]: The Six Psalms are divided into two parts [by] "Glory, Both now," "Alleluia" (3), "Glory to Thee, O God" (3), "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Glory, Both now"; and then the typikons prescribe for the Priest to recite with uncovered head the Morning Prayers before the Holy Doors; however, because now the Six Psalms are recited without interruption, the Priest begins to recite the prayers already at the beginning of the Six Psalms. Therefore also the censing, which was prescribed in previous typikons at the first three psalms, does not exist with us, and has not for a long time, for it is no longer mentioned in the Pochaiv Sluzhebnik (lit. "Service Book").
[^24]: E. g., St. John the Theologian, if it falls on the Sunday of the Holy Fathers.
[^25]: E. g., on Sunday after Nativity.
[^26]: E. g., Menaion December 29.
[^27]: In the Greek Euchologion only one exclamation Οτι ευλογητοα /"For blessed is"/ is given, the same one both on Sunday and on Feasts; the Greeks do not have "Magnifications" here, for they are an invention of the Slavs.
[^28]: When the first antiphon of Tone 4 must be sung, it is not proper to add to it the third troparion of the second antiphon, as some do, but it is sufficient to sing only the first antiphon with the refrain Glory, Both now before its third troparion.
[^29]: So it is presented in the Latin compilation approved in Rome. However, the Ruthenian text prescribes for the Priest to hold in his hand the cross intended for kissing; if someone wants to do so, then let someone else hold the vessel with oil.
[^30]: E. g., Μηναιον /Menaion/ 11, 15, 16, 17, 18 September.
[^31]: Because regarding the troparia of the canon the text of the Synod is somewhat unclear, therefore, adhering on the whole to the essence, we have presented it here in a simplified manner.
[^32]: At Great Matins.
[^33]: Pochaiv Octoechos, Tone 4, Wednesday.
[^34]: Likewise in the Tserkovne Oko, in the 2nd chapter: "But we recite its heirmos, which the Priest begins in a loud voice in the sanctuary; here they have the custom that the Priest, instead of the heirmos, exclaims: 'The Theotokos in songs let us magnify'." The Typikon of the Greek Euchologia on Feasts prescribes for the Deacon to sing the beginning of the heirmos: Ψάλλει ο διάκονος μεγαλοφωνως: "Την θεοτοκον και μητέρα του φωτός εν υμνοις μεγαλυνωμεν", και στιχολογειται η Τιμιότερα; ει δε μη, ψάλλει την αρχήν του ειρμού της Ι5. της εορτής /The Deacon sings very loudly: "The Theotokos and Mother of the Light let us magnify in songs," and "More honorable" is recited (read, or sung); if not, then he sings the beginning of the heirmos of the 9th ode of the Feast/. In the Order of Matins.
[^35]: E. g. January 11 and 17.
[^36]: E. g. December 6 and January 25 and 30.
[^37]: Sometimes also according to the Greeks. February 7 and 8.
[^38]: The Greek Heirmologion also presents: Ει μεν ουκ εστί Κυριακή, μετά τον Ειρμον το Αξιον εστίν; ει δε Κυριακή, μετά την Καταβασιαν συνακτη, το Αγιος Κύριος ο θεός ημών /If it is not Sunday, after the Heirmos -- "It is truly meet"; but if it is Sunday, after the Katavasia the Small Litany, "Holy is the Lord our God"/. Ed. Propag. 1876. Regarding the troparion "Holy is the Lord our God," neither the ancient Greek Typikons nor the Euchologia prescribe to take it three times, nor do they adduce its verses. However, the Slavonic rubrics and the new Constantinopolitan Typikon prescribe to take it three times; regarding the verses -- they do not agree. Our Sluzhebnik and the new Constantinopolitan Typikon present only one verse; ours: "Exalt ye the Lord our God, and worship at His footstool, for He is holy" (5th verse of the 98th psalm, from the last verse of which this troparion is taken). Constantinopolitan: Υψουτε Κυριον τον θεον ημών /Exalt ye the Lord our God/. The Tserkovne Oko and following it the Moscow Typikons present two verses, namely: 1. "For holy is the Lord our God"; 2. "Over all people is our God." In our opinion, if the troparion must be taken three times, then one verse is not sufficient; therefore it is possible to divide the verse "Exalt ye" into two parts, of which the second would begin from: "And worship at His footstool" etc.
[^39]: In the Greek Horologia the given addition refers only to the first verse.
[^40]: For the Pochaiv Sluzhebnik of 1744 also presents censing here only "if it is Sunday or a Feast."
[^41]: Let it be known that besides the Great Forty Days there exist two other periods in which the rubric of the Menaion on September 21 prescribes also a 3rd Sessional Hymn with a Small Litany and a Kathisma before it. The first period lasts from the Apodosis of the Feast of the Holy Cross, which falls on September 21, to the Forefeast of the Nativity of Christ, which falls on December 20 exclusively. The second lasts from the Apodosis of the Feast of Theophany to Cheese-fare Sunday exclusively, that is in these two periods, in which at Sunday Matins the Polyeleos is given. However, in the content of our Psalter three Sessional Hymns and three Kathismata are given only in the Great Forty Days, so we use them.
[^42]: That is, the troparion of the Saint is taken, and then -- Glory, Both now: troparion of the Feast; if two Saints, then troparion of the first Saint, Glory: of the second, Both now: of the Feast.
[^43]: Sometimes inclusive, as October 23 and July 25; sometimes exclusively, that is beginning from the Praises (Pochaiv Anthologion November 12 and December 4, Greek Menaion September 23). In the first case the Katavasia will be the current one after every ode, in the second -- the heirmos of the last canon after the 3rd, 6th, 8th and 9th. ________________________________________
[^44]: In the general church rubric, not a single instance is encountered of a Saint with an All-Night Vigil falling in an Afterfeast on a Sunday, except in the midst of the feasts of Pentecost; but because the feasts of Pentecost have separate rubrics, when some Saint with an All-Night Vigil falls in the midst of Pentecost, then the rubric for him must be taken from the third part of this Typikon. However, in time, this case may happen even outside the feasts of Pentecost and a need for a separate rubric will arise; therefore, for the sake of this, we add these two cases to the instances of feasts: that is, a Saint with an All-Night Vigil on a Sunday and on weekdays, and their rubric may serve also in the case of a Patronal Saint.
[^45]: According to the ancient rubric, a saint "on 4" could be of two types: that is, either with a troparion or without a troparion; and when the saint has no troparion, then at Matins, instead of "God is the Lord," "Alleluia" was sung and the divine service had a separate rubric. But in our current Horologia, troparia are given for every day of the month, and therefore at Matins we always sing "God is the Lord," and we limit the "Alleluia" service to Great Lent, as do the Greeks. However, that same Typikon, as also the Menaion, for the feast of St. John the Theologian on May 8, when it falls on a Sunday of the Holy Fathers, prescribes taking 4 troparia at "God is the Lord", so we do not know why it would not be possible to take 4 at Vespers as well.
[^51]: Lviv Synod; Tserkovne Oko also mentions the saint, but the Stratyn Sluzhebnik of Balaban mentions only the saint with a Doxology.
[^52]: Horologions and Greek Octoechoi do not give a Canon to the Theotokos at Compline; however, the Greek Typikon states, saying: Παρελαβομεν δε και κατ εκαστην εν τοις Αποδειπνοις ψαλλειν Κανόνας Παρακλητικούς της Υπεραγιας Θεοτόκου. (Καιφ. ι) /And we have received [the tradition] to sing daily at Compline the Paraklesis Canons of the Most Holy Theotokos (chapter 10)/. These canons are not found in ordinary Greek Octoechoi, only at the end in them are given two theotokia canons.
[^53]: Our Horologions in the order of Small Compline and Pochaiv Octoechos in Tone 1; Moscow Octoechos gives a Kontakion (in Tone 5, at Compline). Greek Horologions give only the troparion of the saint, whose day it is, or (it must be understood, if the saint has no troparion) troparia: "(Thy Church, O Lord), throughout all the world", Glory: "With the saints give rest", Both now: "Through the intercessions of all the saints", which are found also in our Horologions for use on weekdays.
[^54]: Our Horologions at the end of Matins; Horologions of others do not have "Glory to Thee, O Christ God", but "Glory, Both now", "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Bless".
[^55]: Moscow Typikon in chapter 52 and Peremyshl, page 80.
[^56]: These Sessional Hymns, whether there be one or two (in different editions), end with their own theotokion. And when there is one, then "Glory, Both now" is sung to its theotokion together; when two, then to the second is sung "Glory", and to the theotokion -- "Both now", as is given in the Lviv editions of 1765 and 1897 and in the Greek-Venetian of 1885; but according to general editions, to the second is sung one of the two Sunday verses, given with the two Praises stichera, that is after the 1st Kathisma -- "Arise", after the 2nd -- "I will praise", and to the theotokion -- "Glory, Both now" together, as is given in the Pochaiv Octoechos of 1880, Moscow 1782 and Greek Typikon Καιφ. β /chapter 2/.
[^57]: In our Irmologions, three more small troparia are added to the Polyeleos, that is, one -- Trinitarian with the refrain "Glory", the second -- Theotokion with the refrain "Both now", and after "Alleluia, alleluia, alleluia", "Glory to Thee, O God" thrice -- yet another theotokion. But because this addition does not exist in Greek rubrics, nor in Slavonic ones, nor in the Typikon of the Lviv Synod, but is generally used among us, we also present it.

[^61]: Peremyshl Typikon, page 81. -- Usually typikons give for the 6th Ode only one Kontakion-Ikos of the first service, other services, if they have any of this (for in the Menaion they never have an Ikos, nor ever a Kontakion), are transferred to the 3rd Ode before the Sessional Hymn; e. g. May 8, when it falls on the Sunday of the Holy Fathers, September 20, November 23, December 4. If there be several Sessional Hymns, then "Glory" is sung to the last one, and "Both now" to its theotokion (Menaion, December 4; Lviv Synod, in the Order of Great Matins).
[^62]: Moscow Typikon in chapter 5. Pochaiv Octoechos does not give the Cross-Resurrection canon, but gives: "Sunday on 4, of the Theotokos on 2, and to the saint on 6" (at the end). However, of the Theotokos must be on 4, as in the case of a Polyeleos saint on 6, when the Cross-Resurrection canon is also not taken.
[^63]: Moscow Typikon, chapter 5 and Μαρκ. Καιφ. 90 /Mark, chapter 90/.
[^64]: Lviv Synod, in the Order of the Hours.
[^65]: Peremyshl Typikon, page 81. -- According to the ancient typikon there was to be a Sunday troparion at all hours, also "Glory" at the 1st and 6th -- Goes also to the first saint, at the 3rd and 9th -- to the second; Kontakia -- alternating: at the 1st and 6th -- to the first, at the 3rd and 9th -- to the second saint (compare John the Theologian on the Sunday of the Holy Fathers). When the Kontakion is only for one saint, then it alone is taken at all [hours]; and when for neither, nor for the feast, then the Hypakoe of the tone is taken; for general Greek editions do not have Sunday Kontakia. Regarding the Hypakoe, you have the rubric in Greek Horologions at the 1st Hour, it and at the other hours must be observed.
[^66]: Lviv Synod in heading 5. According to the Typikon given at the end of our Apostles, and in our previous ones, as also in some Greek service books in Goar, the daily antiphons "It is good" are given, also on Sundays, with the refrain only Sunday on the 3rd antiphon, as the Italo-Greeks also observe. General Greek service books give the Typika on Sunday, and Octoechoi also on weekdays; for in them are given daily stichera on the "Beatitudes", by which is understood the presence of the Typika. With such a difference of typikons let everyone preserve the custom of his Church, and among us the Typikon is -- of the Synod. In vain during the Synod some tried, saying, that to take daily antiphons, instead of the Typika, does not correspond to our rite; for daily antiphons are given not only by the aforementioned service books and apostles, but also by Greek Readers [Anagnostiki] and the Moscow Typikon in chapter 25, and St. Sophronius himself, Patriarch of Jerusalem, in the 7th century, in the explanation of the Divine Liturgy (Spicileg. Rom. tom. 4, nn. 12, 13, 14. Propag. 1840) -- mentions nothing about the Typika, but only about the antiphons "It is good". About the Typika we assume that they were left for the case when there is no Liturgy. For in the beginning numerous in monasticism were of the laity, who could not serve the Holy Liturgy; and therefore, instead of the Liturgy, they had to use the Order of Typika; therefore also the Synod limits them to days in which there is no Liturgy, so that in this way the memory of them was preserved only in monasteries. It is equally good to use antiphons, as also the Typika, when it is taken fully; but when from every psalm only one verse is taken and without stichera on the "Beatitudes", as they practice, then it is better to use antiphons. Finally, the full Typika is quite long and in present times was shortened.
[^67]: Our Sluzhebnik on Sundays from the second to the ninth after the Descent of the Holy Spirit.
[^68]: Moscow Typikon in chapter 3 and Peremyshl, page 79.
[^69]: Troparia and other changeable parts of the Liturgy, according to the previous typikon, were not to be taken only of the Sunday, but also of the saint, if he has anything. (e. g. Μαρκ. Καιφ. ξη. and on verso. /Mark, chapters 68 and 79/; as also our Menaion September 7, if it falls on a Sunday). In previous typikons the saint sometimes did not have a troparion, and sometimes also a Kontakion; sometimes he had either only a troparion, or only a Kontakion, sometimes also a Prokimenon-Alleluia and Apostle and Gospel, and Communion Hymn. However, because later among us troparia and Kontakia were added to all saints, that in the sequence of the Menology, services to a saint without Polyeleos at the Liturgy are not taken; the Greeks, in the case of a saint who has an Apostle-Gospel on a Sunday began taking the Apostle only to the saint, and the Gospel -- only of the Sunday. New Constantinopolitan Typikon, 1851, e. g. September 3. Footnotes
[^70]: Search according to the content given at the beginning of the Psalter. The Psalter is divided into three parts, of which the first covers all weeks from the Sunday of Thomas the Apostle to Great Lent, the second -- Great Lent, the third -- Passion Week. In Bright Week the Psalter is not read.
[^71]: Since the Octoechos gives 6 stichera, and the Typikon does not determine which 3 of the 6 to take, we leave this to the judgment of the Reader. However, to say how it is better, let us first recall that the daily service of the Octoechos is double, that is: on Monday -- Penitential and to the Bodiless [Powers], on Tuesday -- Penitential and to the Forerunner, on Wednesday and Friday -- to the Cross and the Theotokos, on Thursday -- to the Apostles and Nicholas, on Saturday -- to all Saints and the Departed. Thus, in order not to discard either of the two services of the weekday, the Greek Octoechos (Παρακλητική /Parakletike/), printed in the "Propaganda" in 1738, gives from the three stichera of the first service only the two first stichera, and from the three stichera of the second service -- only one, the first. Among us, so that the printed stichera given in the Octoechos do not remain in vain, it would be possible to sing alternating all three stichera of the first service and all three stichera of the second service, that is, one year, odd -- three of the first service, and the second year, even -- three of the second service, or, even better -- one year two first stichera of the first service and one sticheron, the first, of the second service, and the second year -- one sticheron, the third, of the first service and two last of the second service. The Greek Typikon takes nothing from the Octoechos, but only three stichera from the Menaion on 6, repeating each (Καιφ. ε /chapter 5/). The Moscow Typikon takes three first stichera of the Theotokos from the Octoechos, which do not exist in our editions, but we find them in the Greek-Venetian edition; the Moscow Octoechos of 1782 has the same stichera as ours.
[^72]: In the Greek Menaion after the Doxastikon to the saint his Theotokion is also added. If there is no Doxastikon, then only certain most general Theotokia of the Octoechos are indicated by initial words; it is implied that they are known, although the number of Octoechos editions makes their search inconvenient. We cite here some: 1. Θεοτόκε, συ ει ο άμπελος "O Theotokos, Thou Art the vine" (Venetian Octoechos, Tone 6, on the Aposticha); θεον σαρκοΰεντα εκ σου "God incarnate from Thee" (Tone 6, on Saturday, Praises, Moscow edition); Δέσποινα προσδεξαι "O Sovereign Lady, receive" (Tone 8, on Saturday at Matins; Την πασαν ελπίδα "All my hope" (Tone 2, on Thursday, on the Aposticha of Matins). Sometimes the Theotokion is not indicated even by initial words, but is only named generally: θεοτοκιον ομοιον /Theotokion similar/, or only: θεοτοκιον /Theotokion/ (Menaion September 3, August 2); in this case one must select a Theotokion from the Octoechos. Four aforementioned Theotokia are given also on "Lord, I have cried", and on the Aposticha (Menaion November 1 and 3, December 5, July 1). In the last edition of the Venetian Menaion Theotokia are given almost always fully. But among us, at the end of every volume of the Menaion are given all Theotokia that are taken on "Lord, I have cried" and on the Aposticha, and not only for every tone, but also for every day of the week, in order not to repeat the same Theotokia many times. In the Pochaiv Anthologion Theotokia are given only according to the tone, and not also according to the day; and in general services sometimes only the first words are cited, and they themselves are not given.
[^73]: Moscow Typikon, chapter 52, and Peremyshl, page 114.
[^74]: Greek Horologions give only the troparion to the saint, if there be one, if -- not, then the four aforementioned troparia.
[^75]: Μαρκ. Καιφ. οε /Mark, chapter 75/.
[^76]: Moscow Typikon, chapter 52, and Peremyshl, page 115.
[^77]: When two kathismata should be read, and when three, we noted in the note to the Order of Daily Matins on page 41. Regarding small litanies which are read between kathismata and sessional hymns, the Lviv Synod, our Horologions and our Sluzhebnyky (at the end) give them also at Small Matins, and they are used also by the Greek-Melkites (according to the testimony of their patriarch bl. m. Clement Bahous). Conversely, in the Russian Typikon, approved by their Governing Synod (Moscow edition of 1859), in the Order of Daily Matins it is written that the Priest refuses them only at the Vigil and when the memory of saints having a Polyeleos and Doxology is celebrated; similarly also in the new Wallachian-Bucharest Typikon, in which in the Order of Daily Matins is given: "We take sessional hymns from the Octoechos without litanies" (untranslatable); and adds: "In monasteries, usually, between kathismata litanies are taken only on Sunday and when more special saints occur". From the Greek Typikon no conclusion can be made, for in it small litanies are not mentioned neither at Small Matins, nor at Great, nor before the Canon, nor after the Canon. It is assumed in the Typikon that this is known to everyone. From the rubrics of the Greek Triodion, given at Matins on Meatfare Saturday, one can conclude that these litanies should be refused also at Small Matins. For it gives: η συνηιϊης στιχολογια. Εν δε ταις συναπταις πασαις της στιχολογιας και του Κανόνος, μνημονεύονται πάντες οι προαπελΰοντες Πατέρες και αδελφοί ημων /Ordinary Stichology. In all small litanies of the Stichology and of the Canon, all our fathers and brethren who have passed away before us are commemorated/. Let everyone observe the rubric and custom of his Church. Finally, in our opinion, later typikons reject litanies here only for the sake of greater shortening of the divine service; if the single difference between Small and Great Matins were the rejection or use of litanies, then this difference should have been indicated in some place of ancient liturgical books; however, this is not encountered. What the exclamation of the third litany should be is not indicated in any of the church books. Therefore we are forced to borrow it from Great Matins. At Great Matins in Slavonic books two exclamations are given which are used at the third litany, that is one -- for Sunday "For blessed is" and the second -- for Polyeleos feasts "For holy Art Thou". For the sake of distinguishing the Sunday day from the ordinary day, at Small Matins it is appropriate to use the second "For holy Art Thou", although it would not be bad to use also the first "For blessed is" (Οτι ευλογητοα), for in Greek books we find only this one exclamation, without distinction of day. Regarding Sessional Hymns, they are taken two or three after each stichology, depending on the edition, except the Theotokion. In Lviv editions of the Octoechos and in the Greek-Venetian one, only to the Theotokion is sung "Glory, Both now". In the Pochaiv and Moscow ones a separate refrain is also given to every second, or even to the third sessional hymn. This refrain, corresponding to the content of the sessional hymn: on Monday and Tuesday -- Penitential "O Lord, rebuke me not in Thine anger"; on Wednesday and Friday -- of the Cross, and on Thursday -- of the Apostles; to the third sessional hymn, that is the Martyron -- also the Martyron refrain: "Wondrous is God in His saints".

Ει δ ουν βουλει, είπε και Αποστιχον της Οκτωηχου /Do not wonder about the Great Doxology; for it is permitted, as he who wrote the Typikon says, even when the Octoechos is sung, and as we saw in another Typikon, of that called Let us sing to the Lord, to perform the Great Doxology. And if you wish, say also the Aposticha of the Octoechos/.

[^91]: The Greek Typikon gives the whole service only to the saint, and Apostle and Gospel -- first of the day, and then of the saint; Προκειμενον του κατά την ημεραν Αγιου, Αλληλούια του Αγιου, Ευαγγελιον της ημέρας και του Αγιου. (Καιφ. σ) /Prokimenon of the saint of the day, Alleluia of the saint, Gospel of the day and of the saint (chapter 6)/. So also in chapter 99, Mark. Although this rubric is given only in the Saturday service, however, it must be understood that also on other days of the week it should be so. Slavonic typikons prescribe the whole service to the day and to the saint, if he has one, and troparia -- also to the temple, if it is of the Lord or of the Theotokos. The Moscow Typikon also prescribes to the temple, if the temple is of a saint (although this does not agree with the rubric of that same Typikon, given on September 26 and January 30); this same Typikon ends the Kontakia with the Kontakion for the Dead "With the saints give rest" with the refrain "Glory" and the Kontakion of the temple, if it is of the Lord or of the Theotokos, if -- not, then with the usual "Protection" ("O Undisputed Intercessor") with the refrain "Both now" (chapter 52). This custom we find also among Greek-Italians and Greek-Melkites, but it does not exist among Constantinopolitan Greeks and Athonites, with the exception of some. But, since according to the rubric of the Greek Typikon, two Apostles and two Gospels were to be taken, and according to the Slavonic rubric, also the whole service of the day and of the saint, if he has one, and, since many saints (over one hundred eighty) have an Apostle and Gospel, as follows from the content of the Apostle-Gospel, therefore, in order to shorten the duration of the divine service, followers of the Greek Rite began already many years ago to reject certain rubrics; therefore also our Ruthenians take at the Liturgy only the service of the day, and reject the saint without Polyeleos; some -- conversely: take only the service to the saint, and reject the service of the day, as evidenced by the Pochaiv Sluzhebnik of 1765, which gives the Apostle and Gospel only on Sundays, and on weekdays -- only in Bright Week and in the week after the Descent of the Holy Spirit, similarly as Latin Missals, which give the Apostle and Gospel of the day only in these two mentioned weeks, for Great Lent and for certain other days. This custom we find also among Greek-Italians, observed also by some of those who are called Orthodox, whom the Moscow Typikon accuses, saying: "The Ecumenical Church does not take neither on the Beatitudes, nor at Liturgies the Apostle and Gospel to the saint on every day, only the sequential, that is the pillar throughout the whole year, in sequence, as also of selected saints who have an Apostle and Gospel. And if the Apostle and Gospel of the saint is read every day, then this is from one's own ignorance, and not according to the church typikon" (chapter 58, at the end). Exactly so also in the manuscript of the three-hundred-year-old Gospel that is among us. However, this rubric of the Ecumenical Church is not observed by the Constantinopolitan Hierarch, called Ecumenical, nor by the Churches subject to him, who (according to the testimony of hierarch Benjamin Νεαπολεος /of Neapolis/, who lived in Constantinople and on Mount Athos, who in our times accepted church union) have the custom, also in monasteries, to take the Apostle and Gospel only of the day, if the saint does not have one, if he has, then only to the saint, and in another they adhere to the new Constantinopolitan Typikon, printed in the patriarchal typography in 1851, marked with the patriarchal seal and confirmed by signatures of all patriarchs and hierarchs subject to them. In this Typikon there, where the rubric gives two Apostles and Gospels, one Apostle-Gospel is given, that is the Apostle -- of the first service, and the Gospel -- of the second service. Thus e. g. October 26, November 21, when they fall on a Sunday and on John the Theologian May 8, when it falls on Ascension.

When someone reads in the weeks the Apostle and Gospel only to the saint, or only for a certain intention, does not need to take it also to the feast, but only then, when he reads the Apostle-Gospel of the day.
[^197]: About the commemoration of the feast at the Dismissal in the Afterfeast we find nothing in Greek typikons. From the Typikon of Slavonic Triodia and of the Moscow Typikon one could conclude that the commemoration of the feast should be taken only on the very solemn day of the feast and on its Apodosis. For it prescribes to take the Paschal Dismissal throughout the whole Bright Week, every day of which has the form of the divine service of the very day of the Resurrection, and afterwards prescribes to take it at the Liturgy of the Apodosis of the Resurrection. However, today we observe the general custom to make the festal commemoration also on other days of the Afterfeast, which has also the rubric of the Sluzhebnik, printed in Stratyn under the Lviv Bishop Gedeon Balaban in 1604, 11 years before the Tserkovne Oko, which gives the following: "Know, that festal dismissals are taken from the day of the feast until the Apodosis of the feast of every day" (page 517). Similarly one could take in Theotokion Afterfeasts, but the words "today" and "solemnly" must be discarded. However, in Afterfeasts of the Lord it is better not to take the commemoration of the feast on Sunday, for it does not combine well with the Sunday commemoration, which must occupy the first place. It would be, e. g. on the Afterfeast of the Nativity of Christ: "Who rose from the dead and Who was born in a cavern in Bethlehem of Judea and let Himself be laid in a manger for our salvation, Christ, our true God". And on weekdays, except Sunday, the commemoration of the feast can be taken without doubt, for then the service of the feast replaces the service of the Octoechos and therefore, instead of the commemoration of the service of the day, that is of the Octoechos, it is good to take the commemoration of the service of the feast. Some on Sunday discard the Sunday commemoration and take only of the feast, but they act contrary to our Sluzhebnyky, which on the Sunday of the Holy Fathers, in the middle of the feast of the Ascension before Pentecost, give the Sunday commemoration.

[^201]: According to the most general and most ancient typikons in the Afterfeast and on the Apodosis the Trisagion should be taken, and not "As many as have been baptized into Christ" or "Before Thy Cross", for they are taken on the very day of the feast, with the exception of "As many as have been baptized into Christ", which is taken not only on the very day of the Resurrection, but also throughout the whole Bright Week, since throughout the whole Bright Week the divine service takes place as on the very day of the Resurrection. On other days, until the Apodosis of the Resurrection, the Trisagion is taken. So have the general Greek and Slavonic typikons and the most ancient Typikon of the Monastery of St. Nicholas of Casole in the district of Otranto, kept in the Barberini library in Rome, written six hundred or seven hundred years ago. In it on fol. 121 and 124 is given the Typikon, which I gave. [^263]: In the Greek Typikon and the Slavic one of the Lviv University nothing is said about this bringing out of the precious Cross, except the Troparion "Save, O Lord"; Απέρχεται ο Ιερεύς και ο Εκκλησιαρχης συν τω Κανδηλαπτη εν τω σκευοφυλακιω μετά λαμπάδων και θυμιατών, και λαμβανουσιν το τιμιον ξυλον του Σταυρου, ψάλλοντες και το Τροπαριον Σωσον Κύριε τον λαον σου, και φερουσιν εις την Εκκλησιαν, και επιτνθεασιν αυτό επάνω της αγίας Τραπέζης, και απτει κηρος έμπροσθεν αυτό επάνω της αγίας Τραπέζης, και απτει κηρος έμπροσθεν δι όλης της νυκτός/The Priest and the Ecclesiarch with the lamp-lighter go to the sacristy with candles and censers and take the precious wood of the Cross, singing the troparion "Save, O Lord, Thy people", carry it to the church and place it on the holy table, and a candle is lit before it for the whole night/. (14 September). The beginning is usual and other preparatory prayers, that is Trisagion with "Our Father", as later Slavic typikons give, longer than this entire order, for it consists only of one Troparion of the Cross, and with the Slavic addition, also of a Kontakion.
[^264]: Ancient Greek typikons mention nothing about a Deacon, neither at the bringing out, nor at the exaltation, nor at the laying of the precious Cross, but only about one priest. The Greek typikon, similarly to the Slavic ones, prescribes for the Priest to vest in all priestly vestments: αλασσει ο Ιερεύς πασαν την ιερατικην στολην /the Priest vests in all priestly vestments/. The Greek Triodion (Sunday of the Veneration of the Cross) and the new Constantinopolitan Typikon, similarly to Slavic typikons, prescribes for the Priest to enter with the cross from the sanctuary to the temple through the northern doors: εκ του αριστερού Βήματος /from the left side of the sanctuary/. Greek typikons, with the exception of the new Constantinopolitan, and the Slavic of the Lviv University, prescribe for the Priest, having exited from the sanctuary to the temple, to head to the entrance doors that lead from the temple to the narthex, which are sometimes called royal, and there await the end of the Doxology and from there exclaim "Wisdom, attend", and then head to the tetrapod, which is before the iconostasis. Although these doors are called royal, βασιλικαι /royal/, one must understand that they were called so in the past. Today we call royal the middle doors of the iconostasis, which according to ancient custom are called holy: αγιαι ΰυραι /holy doors/ (chapter 96, Greek Typikon).
[^265]: According to the Slavic typikon or, speaking more precisely, according to the Pochaiv Menaion, according to the Moscow Typikon and according to the Tserkovne Oko, the Deacon sings the whole litany, and the Priest sings nothing. And the censer, which with us the Priest holds with the cross, it would be better for the Deacon to hold and cense, as the new Constantinopolitan Typikon and the Tserkovne Oko prescribe on 14 September.
[^266]: From the aforesaid we see that with us, according to the Typikon of the Lviv University, the Priest turns first to the east, then to the north, after that to the west, to the south and again to the east. According to general Slavic typikons: to the east, to the west, to the south, to the north and again to the east. According to the Greek Typikon: to the east, to the south, to the west, to the north and again to the east. The new Constantinopolitan Typikon prescribes as with us.
[^267]: The rule of the Triodion of the Sunday of the Veneration of the Cross prescribes for the Priest before the veneration to open the reliquary of the cross: και ανοιξας την ύηκην /and, having opened the repository/, and in the Typikon of the Lviv University: "And after the opening of the reliquary of the cross". From this it follows that they had particles of the precious Cross in monasteries. The Greek Typikon and two handwritten Slavic ones that you have, do not prescribe for the Priest to sing separately "Before Thy Cross", but for the choirs; nor to bow to the precious Cross to the ground; for only the Tserkovne Oko prescribes this on 14 September.
[^268]: The Greek Typikon prescribes before the kissing of the Cross three prostrations, and after the kissing -- one; and Slavic ones -- before the kissing -- two, and after the kissing -- one; however, today we make only one before and one after the kissing. Also the Greek Typikon, having discarded both last litanies, immediately after the veneration gives the dismissal: Ψαλλομενης δε της μεγάλης δοξολογίας, αλασσει ο Ιερεύς πασαν την ιερατικην στολην, και εισέρχεται μετά του θυμιατού, προηγουμένων των λαμπάδων, εν τη αγία Τρεπεζη, και Ουμιων τον αγιον σταυρόν σταυροειδως, αίρει αυτόν μετά δίσκου επί καιφαλης, και προπορευόμενων δυο λαμπάδων, φέρει αυτόν μέχρι των βασιλικών πυλών του ναού, κακεισαι ισταται. Και πληρουμενης της δοξολογίας και του τρισάγιου, λέγει ο Ιερεύς μεγαλόφωνος: Σοφια ορθοί. Και αρχόμενα του τροπαρίου Σωσον Κύριε, και ούτως εισοδευει μετά του αγίου σταυρού, και ούτως ευτρεπισμενου τετραποδιου, τνθεται ο τίμιος σταυρός επάνω αυτού, και Ουμια ο Ιερεύς σταυροειδως. ЕІ6 ούτως βολών μετανοίας τρεις, καν ποια εστίν ήμερα, και λαβών ανά χείρας τον τιμιον σταυρόν γυμνον μετά βασιλικών κλάδων, ισταται έμπροσθεν του τετραποδιου, βλέπων κατ ανατολάς, και λέγει εις επηκοον πάντων: Ελεησον ημάς ο Θεός. Και αρχόμενα της πρώτης εκατοντάδας το Κύριε ελεησον, σφραγίζοντας του Ιερέως εν ταις εναρξεσιν μετά του αγίου σταυρού. Είτα κλίνει την καιφαλην όσον σπιύαμην από της γης, και καταμικρον ανισταται άχρι συμπληρωσεος της εκατοντάδας. Ηνικα δε φθάσει ενς το 97 Κύριε ελεησον, υψοι την φωνην ο Εκκλησιαρχης, ήγουν το Κύριε ελεησον τρις, και αισθομενος ο Ιερεύς τέλος λαμβάνειν την εκατοντάδα, σφραγίζει πάλιν τρις. Είτα στραφείς επί το νοτιον μέρος, λέγει: Ετι δεομεβα... και αρχόμενα της δευτέρας εκατοντάδας, και ποιεί ο Ιερεύς την δεύτερον υψωσιν, ως προγεγραπται. Ειύ ούτως στραφείς επί δυσμάς λέγει: Ετι δεομεθα, και αρχόμενα της τρίτης εκατοντάδας. Πληρωμένης δε αυτής, στρέφεται ο Ιερεύς επί το βορειον μέρος, και λέγει: Ετι δεομεθα... και γίνεται η τετάρτη υψωσις. Και ούτως στρέφεται ο Ιερεύς κατ ανατολάς, και λέγει: Ετι δεομεύα... και αρχομεΟα της πέμπτης εκατοντάδας. Μετά δε την πεμπτην υψωσιν ψαλλομεν το Κοντακιον Ο υψωθείς. ЕІІ9 ούτως: Τον σταυρόν σου προσκυνουμεν Δέσποτα τρεις. Ψαλλόντων δε των αδελφών, αποτι6ισιν ο Ιερεύς το τιμιον ξυλον εν τετραποδιω, και αρχόμενα προσκυνειν, ο τε Ιερεύς, και ο Προεστως, ποιουντες και μετανοίας τρεις κατενωπιον του τυμιου σταυρού, είτα ασπάζονται. Και μετά το ασπαζαστ)αι βαλλουσιν μιαν μετανοιαν; ειΰ ούτως εις τους χορούς δεξιά και αριστερά. Είτα εισέρχονται οι αδελφοί δυο δυο κατά ταξιν, και προσκυνουσι και ασπάζονται ομοίως. Ψαλλομεν δε και τα στιχηρα ιδιομελα, αχρις ουν προσκυνουσιν οι αδελφοί, εις ηχον β το Δεύτε πιστοί. Και μετά το προσκυνησαι παντός λέγει ο Ιερεύς: Σοφια, και Απολυσις /During the singing of the Great Doxology the Priest vests in all priestly vestments and proceeds with the censer, preceded by candle-bearers, to the holy table. Having censed the holy cross crosswise, he takes it with the diskos on his head and, preceded by two candle-bearers, carries it to the royal doors of the temple, remaining there. At the end of the Doxology and Trisagion, the Priest loudly exclaims: "Wisdom, attend!" and we begin the troparion "Save, O Lord". The Priest enters with the holy cross and places the precious cross on the prepared tetrapod, having censed it crosswise. Then, having bowed three times, whatever day it may be, he takes into his hands the precious cross, wrapped with basil branches, stands before the tetrapod, looking to the east, and says so that all can hear: "Have mercy on us, O God". And we begin "Lord, have mercy" of the first hundred, and the Priest at the beginning blesses with the holy cross. After this he bows his head to, approximately, a quarter of a meter from the ground and gradually rises until the end of the hundred. When "Lord, have mercy" is sung for the 97th time, the Ecclesiarch raises his voice. Then "Lord, have mercy" is sung three times, and the Priest, noticing that the hundred is coming to an end, again signs three times with the cross. Then he, having turned to the south, says: "Again we pray" and we begin the second hundred, and the Priest performs the second exaltation of the cross, as prescribed. Then, turned to the west, says: "Again we pray" and we begin the third hundred. At the end, the Priest turns to the north and says: "Again we pray" and the fourth exaltation takes place. Then the Priest turns to the east and says: "Again we pray" and we begin the fifth hundred. After the fifth exaltation we sing the Kontakion "Thou Who Wast lifted up" ("Voznesyisya"). Then "Before Thy Cross" is sung three times. While the brethren sing, the Priest places the precious cross on the tetrapod and we begin to venerate. The Priest and the Superior, having bowed three times before the precious cross, kiss it. After kissing they bow once. Also those in the choirs on the right and left. Then the brethren approach two by two, according to rank, bowing, simultaneously and kiss. We sing the stichera idiomesa, while the brethren venerate, in Tone 2 "Come, ye faithful". And when all have finished venerating, the Priest exclaims: "Wisdom!" and the dismissal follows/ (14 September).

[^272]: Thus our Pochaiv Menaion, Tserkovne Oko and Moscow Typikon. But our liturgikons, horologia and the Greek-Venetian Menaion of 1755 prescribe to take the Service of the Holy Fathers on the Sunday following 11 October; one must understand, that when 11 October falls on a weekday; similarly in the latest Greek-Venetian Menaion (1884) and in the new Constantinopolitan Typikon, where it is prescribed to take on the very day of 11 October, if Sunday, if -- not, then on the following Sunday. What shall we say to this? We consider that all these rules are good, however, it is not good when liturgical books of one and the same church province give uncoordinated rules. For when we accept the rule of our Menaion, then let it be placed also in the liturgikons And in the horologia, for when we accept the rule of the latter, then let It be also in the Menaion. And if we adhere to the rule of the Menaion, then it is necessary to present it already on 8 October, so that, reading, one can notice about the Following Sunday. This must be understood also about the Service of the Holy Fathers of the First Six Councils on 16 July, which the menaia both ours and Greek, Prescribe to transfer back, to 13 July, if it falls on Wednesday; the Greek menaia present this not in accordance with their rule on 11 October, when they prescribe to transfer this service from 16 July back, they have to transfer it back also from 11 October. It seems to us, And it would be simpler not to transfer these services back, but to take on the very [days of] 11 October and 16 July, when they fall on Sunday, if -- not, on the following Sunday.

[^277]: Some consider, according to the edition of the Peremyshl Typikon of 1870, p. 271, that neither on St. Michael, nor on St. Prophet Elias, should "Blessed is the man" be sung and, that then not a single kathisma is taken, for this kathisma, as the publisher writes about it, is found only in the Pochaiv Anthologion, and in the most ancient menaia and Anthologia they are not mentioned; the reason for this is considered to be that "Elias did not die, and St. Michael, as bodiless, is not subject to death". However, this is not enough. For regarding the rule, not only the Pochaiv Anthologion (Anthologion) of 1777 and the Pochaiv Menaion of the same year, but also the Lviv Anthologion (Anthologion) of 1643 and the Great Typikon, under the title Tserkovne Oko, printed in Moscow in 1615, that is more than a century and a half before the Pochaiv Anthologion, and the manuscript Anthologion of 1736, which we have, and the Typikon of the All-Russian Church, printed in Moscow in 1859, by the decision of its Governing Synod, give also on these two feasts the kathisma "Blessed is the man". Although some rules, like the Moscow Menaion of 1782, the Greek-Venetian of 1884 do not give "Blessed is the man", it does not follow from this that no kathisma is needed, for even on Saints without Polyeleos in the Menaion a kathisma is not given, but the sequential one is meant; so here one can understand the sequential one, which three ancient handwritten Slavic typikons give: one -- of the Lviv University, the second -- of St. Onuphrius in Lviv, and the third -- of the library of the Chapter of St. George; also Tserkovne Oko (which gives two rules: one with "Blessed is the man", and the second with the sequential kathisma). The reason that these rules give for these two feasts a sequential kathisma, may lie in the fact that their service initially had neither All-Night Vigil nor Polyeleos, but gradually, with time, grew into All-Night Vigil. About St. Elias it is written in the Pochaiv Menaion: "Let it be known that in printed Greek menaia, in handwritten typikons, and also in Slavic handwritten and printed typikons, the service of the Prophet Elias is given on 6, with Octoechos". And regarding St. Michael, the above-mentioned Slavic typikons give him a service only of the Polyeleos type, but incomplete, for they partially combine his service with the service of the Octoechos, as for a Saint without Polyeleos.

[^279]: We find the Service of St. Catherine as having Polyeleos only in our Pochaiv Menaion and in the new Greek-Venetian one; but in others -- without Polyeleos. In later Greek typikons we find it given on 25 November with the Apodosis of the Feast of the Entry into the Temple of the Most Holy Theotokos, and in earlier ones -- on the 24th, as it is today among Greek-Slavs. Thus the Greek-Venetian Menaion of 1615 gives: Σημειωσαι ουν, ότι ευρομεν εν τισι Τυπικοις των νεωτέρων, ότι εν τιοα των πόλεων ψαλλεται η ακολουθία της αγίας μάρτυρος Αικατερίνης εν τη κε του μηνός, εν η και αποδιδοται η εορτή. Εν ετεροις δε Τυπικοις παλαιοτεροις ευρομεν αυτήν εορτάζεσαι εν τη κδ του αυτού μηνός: εν δε τη κε ψαλλομεν την ακολουθίαν του εν αγιοις Κλημεντος Παπα Ρώμης, και Πέτρου Αλεξανδρείας, εν η και αποδιδοται η εορτή των Εισοδιων /Note, therefore, that we found in some newer typikons, that in some places the service of the holy martyr Catherine is sung on the 25th day of this month, on which the feast is also given up. In other older typikons we found that her memory is celebrated on the 24th of this month, and on the 25th we sing the service of Saints Clement Pope of Rome and Peter of Alexandria, and on this day also the feast of the Entry is given up/. This transfer from the 24th to the 25th day, in the opinion of the Greeks, as explained by the new Greek-Venetian Menaion (24 November, p. 158), was done at the wish of the monks of Mount Sinai, so that it would not coincide with the Apodosis of the feast and, so that in this way the memory of the saint would be honored more solemnly. For we know that the body of the holy great martyr was transferred by angelic power to Mount Sinai and buried there.

[^337]: Greek menaia and typikons give a rule only for two cases of Saturdays and Sundays between the Nativity and Theophany, that is: one -- for two Saturdays and two Sundays; the second -- for one Saturday and one Sunday, and for these one Saturday and one Sunday they give the following rule: Ει δε τύχη εν Σαββατον και μια Κυριακή, αναγινωσκεται τω μεν Σαββατω, Σαββατω μετά την Χρίστου γεννησιν, τη δε Κυριακή, Κυριακή προ των Φοτων /If there should happen to be one Saturday and one Sunday, on the Saturday is read that which is also on the Saturday after the Nativity of Christ, and on the Sunday that which is on the Sunday before Theophany/. And this rule is enough for the case of one Saturday with one Sunday, for then this Saturday falls during December (the 31st), and the Sunday -- during January (the 1st); however, it is not enough for one Saturday with two Sundays, nor for one Sunday with two Saturdays, for then this Saturday falls during January (the 1st), as in the seventh row, and the Sunday -- during December (the 31st), as this is in the 3rd row; and as it is not possible, according to the Greek Typikon itself, to read the Apostle-Gospel of the Sunday after the Nativity outside the feast of the Nativity, in January, but it must be transferred back, to 26 December δια το αρχήν λαμβάνειν τον Ιαννουαριον μήνα, και την των Χρίστου Γεννών εορτην αποδιδοσΟαι /because the month of January begins and the feast of the Nativity of Christ is given up/: so it is not possible to read the Apostle-Gospel of the Sunday before Theophany, within the feast of the Nativity, or the Apostle-Gospel of the Saturday after the Nativity to read in January. Therefore there is nothing strange that the Slavs supplemented their rules with what was lacking. However, the rules of our Menaion and the Russian ones, given on 26 December, for Saturdays and Sundays between the Nativity and Theophany, likely due to the negligence of copyists, in some places gave incorrectly and must be corrected, in our opinion, thus: The rule of the first case: "If the Nativity falls on a Sunday", then it should end thus: "as in the present section in the row it will appear, if the Circumcision and Basil fall on a Sunday" (as in the following case). The rule of the third case, "if the Nativity on Tuesday", then from the words: "And on Sunday" to the end, and should be: "And on Sunday, which is before Theophany, Prokimenon, Apostle, Alleluia and Gospel we read on the first day of January, as will be in the row, if the Circumcision and Basil fall on a Sunday". The rule of the fifth case from the words: "And on the second day Prokimenon, Apostle, Alleluia and Gospel we read first of the Sunday before Theophany, and then -- of the Saint" and everything that is there. The rule prescribes to read in this case at Matins two Gospels: one of the Sunday, and the second -- sequential, we do not know from where it has this, for besides one sequential Sunday Gospel at Matins we know not, because the Sunday before Theophany has nothing at Matins.

[^350]: 1 We find nothing about the tri-candle either in Greek typikons, or in Slavic typikons of non-united Churches, but only in our Ukrainian ones. The typikon does not mention only one and, in this case, all three tri-candles are not immersed simultaneously, but one at each of the three exclamations of the words "Great Art Thou, O Lord", about which also Kulchynsky writes: Trinae candelae accensae immerguntur singulatim in aqua (Specim. Eccl. Ruth. Pars II ad 6 Jan.) /"Lit tri-candles are immersed one by one into the water" (Specimen of the Ruthenian Church, part II, on 6 January)/. [^353]: In Greek typikons it is noted that the troparion "When in Jordan" is sung only once, and only the Priest himself sings it (Euchologion and Menaion). [^354]: Greek typikons order to sprinkle the temple, and our Euchologia -- also the Holy Table. Slavic menaia give the following rule about the sprinkling of monks: "And the Superior, having taken holy water in a bowl and turning his face to the west, holds with his left hand the precious Cross, and with his right -- basil, and sprinkles crosswise on all sides. Then the priests approach first, two by two, and kiss the precious Cross, and the Superior signs them with basil with holy water crosswise on the forehead; in the same way also all the brethren. All sing the troparion many times, until all the brethren are sanctified by the sprinkling with water and kissing". Similarly also the Constantinopolitan Patriarch signs with holy water the hierarchs and church dignitaries (Ορφικιουχους /officials/), as the new Constantinopolitan Typikon gives.

[^410]: Since there are 4 kathismata, that is 3 sequential ones and Polyeleos, the question arises, which litanies should be sung here; for the general rule has only three. To this, since the feast has three sessional hymns, and here only two are given, then which two of the three to sing here? Regarding the litanies, our and Russian typikons mention litanies after the 3rd kathisma, from this it follows that after the 1st and 2nd kathismata there are no litanies, which the Pochaiv Triodion also excludes after the 1st kathisma before the sessional hymn of the Triodion on 25 March; and assuming such, it is proper to take two small litanies: one -- before the post-Polyeleos sessional hymn, with the exclamation "For blessed is Thy name", and the second -- before the sessional hymn of the 3rd kathisma, with the exclamation "For Thou Art good" or "For Thine is the dominion", at choice. But because only the Russian and Romanian typikons do not prescribe the Small Litany at Matins on a weekday, and with us this is not adhered to, therefore we think that here only after the 1st kathisma one need not take a litany, and after the 2nd one should take with the exclamation "For Thine is the dominion", after the 3rd -- with the exclamation "For Thou Art good". And of the two sessional hymns of the feast let one be taken, which is after the Polyeleos, and the second -- one of the first two, at choice.

Finally we consider that the Katavasia in this case should be only after the 3rd, 6th, 8th and 9th odes, namely the heirmos of the last canon, that is after the 3rd, 8th and 9th -- the heirmos of the three-ode canon, and after the 6th -- of the Cross.

[^440]: The Co-suffering of the Most Holy Theotokos can fall up to 20 July, in the case of the latest Pascha, which is 25 April. For from Pascha to the Co-suffering there will be 69 days, that is from Pascha to the Descent -- 50, from the Descent to the Sunday of All Saints and to the following Sunday (of the Eucharist) -- 14, from the second Sunday to the following Friday -- 5 days. If on 25 April there will be Pascha, then the 69th day from Pascha will be 2 July. If the last boundary of Pascha shifts three days back, then the Co-suffering will move to 29 June, and if eight days back, it will move to 24 June.

[^450]: This procession is explained by the Greek Menaion: Προεορτια του τίμιου και ζωοποιού σταυρού, ήτοι η εξελευσις αυτού εκ του βασιλικού παλατιού εις την πολιν / Forefeast of the Precious and Life-giving Cross, that is its true procession from the royal palace to the city/. [^454]: Although Greek typikons do not give the blessing of water on this day, however, this custom, inherent to Greek-Slavs, is taken from the Greeks, who once had the custom of performing the blessing of water at the beginning of each month and, accordingly, on 1 August, according to the testimony of Balsamon in the explanation of Canon V of the Trullan Synod: Haec statuente canone, novilunium quidem festum ante annos omnem memoriam supeantes cessavit; eius loco, Dei gratia, ut et ipse propitious reddatur, preces, as Aquae lustrales in Ecclesia a populo fideli fiunt in uniuscuiusque mensis principio (Asseman. Calend. Tom. I. Cap. XI. Pag. 156) /Establishing this canon, truly the new moon feast, which from ancient times erased all memory of it; in its place, thanks be to God, and better prayers take place, and sanctification of water in the church, which the faithful people perform at the beginning of each month (Assemani, Calend., Vol. III, Part I, Chapter XI, p. 156)/.

Part. 2, p. 8).

[^470]: Both at Vespers and at Matins we take the two litanies "In peace let us pray to the Lord" and, at the end, "Have mercy on us, O God" for the dead, although the rubric of the Triodion does not prescribe this; however, it provides for a Panakhida (Parastas) after Vespers, in which these litanies would be present. Since in reality we do not serve a Panakhida today after Vespers, we say its litanies at least at Vespers and at Matins; although our Horologia (at the end) provide the litany for the dead "Have mercy on us, O God" only at the end of Matins. After the dismissal of this [service], we add also "In blessed falling asleep" just as at the Parastas. At Matins we say the small litanies in their places, that is, after the Kathisma and in the Canon, after Odes 3, 6, and 9; we say the usual ones, and not for the dead, since our Pochaiv Triodion does not prescribe litanies for the dead at that time. Tserkovne Oko and the Moscow Typikon prescribe the litany for the dead after Ode 6. The Greek Triodion prescribes commemorating the dead at the litany after the Kathisma and at all litanies of the Canon: "At all litanies of the Stichology and of the Canon, all our departed fathers and brethren are commemorated". Our Manuscript Typikon agrees with this, in which: the Priest pronounces the petitions; either after the Kathisma or after the Canon he always mentions the dead. The Euchologion of Benedict XIV on the litany for the dead gives the prayer only when it begins with "Have mercy on us, O God", and never if it begins with "Again and again".

[^537]: For some reason on every Saturday the memory of St. Great Martyr Theodore is honored... (Nilles in Eortologion). In Constantinople there was a great cult of one holy martyr... for the sake of the miracle of peace and for the sake of this miracle a more special feast was established, on which the annual memory is celebrated, on the first Saturday of the forty-day fast. Julian the Apostate... 362. St. Theodore the Tyro appeared at night to the Bishop of the imperial city... (Nilles Calend. Part 2, p. 106).

[^542]: Orthodoxy means correct belief, that is the correct faith regarding the veneration of holy icons, which the Iconoclasts destroyed. The Seventh Ecumenical Council (Second of Nicaea) in 787 restored their veneration. Another council, convened in Constantinople in 842, under St. Methodius, with the support of the holy Empress Theodora, ordered the commemoration of this restoration every year on the first Sunday of Great Lent.

[^553]: The Moscow Typikon and the new Athenian Triodion prescribe Katavasia only after the 3rd, 6th, 8th and 9th; but Tserkovne Oko and the Kyiv Triodion of 1640 prescribe Katavasia after each ode, which, we suppose, is more correct, for also on other days, on which the Canon of the Triodion is taken last, it has Katavasia after each ode, as on Meatfare and Cheesefare Saturdays and on Cheesefare Wednesday and Friday (although also for these two days the rubrics of the Triodion are imprecise). [^554]: Kyiv and Lviv Triodia.
[^555]: The Order of the Akathist, that is the Non-Sitting [Hymn], is sung in memory of the triple deliverance of Constantinople from the invasion of enemies, thanks to the intercession of the Mother of God, whose precious robe, brought from Jerusalem and placed by St. Pulcheria in the Blachernae church, and the Icon of the Hodegetria, painted, in the opinion of the Greeks, by St. Luke, were carried around the city, invoking her help. The first invasion was under Emperor Heraclius (reigned from 610 to 641) from the Persian army, led by the satrap Sarvar, and also from the Scythian army, under the command of the Khagan. Part of the enemies were destroyed by a small number of armed Christians who came out of the temple of the Most Holy Theotokos, and partly -- by a strong sea storm which destroyed their ships. The second invasion was 36 years later, that is under Constantine Pogonatos (668-685) and ended partly by the disease of the soldiers, and partly -- by a sea storm when they were returning home. The third was under Leo the Isaurian (717-741) and ended by a sea storm, famine, division of forces against the Bulgarians, by whom they were beaten (Synaxarion of this Saturday, about which also Nilles, Calend. vol. 2, p. 152).
[^556]: Besides the initial Kondakion "To the Directress", the rest of the Akathist consists of 12 Ikos and 12 Kontakia, together -- of 24 members according to the number of 24 letters of the Greek alphabet, with which each member, in the Greek text, begins in sequence.
[^557]: In the Patriarchal Church of Constantinople the Akathist is sung not at Matins, but before that, at Small Compline, that is at "It is truly meet" -- the first station by the Patriarch himself, the second -- after the 3rd Ode of the canon of the feast by the Bishop of Caesarea, the third -- after the 6th Ode by the Bishop of Ephesus, the fourth -- after the 9th Ode by the Bishop of Heraclea (New Constantinopolitan Typikon).
[^558]: The Greek Triodion does not prescribe any censing. Tserkovne Oko and our Manuscript Typikon prescribe 4 censings, as do ours and the Russian rubrics, however, they order to cense only the icons and the brethren, ours and the Russian -- only the icons and the brethren, and at the other three stations -- only the Superior and the choirs. It would be better for us to cense only once, at the beginning.

[^562]: Greek vaïon /palm branch/ means a date branch, that is a palm branch, whence also the Latin Dominica Palmarum /Palm Sunday/, for John 12:13 also says: "Took branches of palm trees", although undoubtedly people cut branches of olive trees, for Christ entered Jerusalem from the Mount of Olives. Where date palms do not grow, there only olive branches are used; and among us, since olives also do not grow, willow branches are used, hence also in Tserkovne Oko: "reciting the prayer over the willow".

[^566]: The service of these days is Passion-Penitential, foretelling the sufferings of Christ the Lord, Who here is presented in the image of the Patriarch Joseph, persecuted by his brothers, and the Jewish synagogue, which is depicted in the image of the unfaithful and adulterous wife of Potiphar; with the addition of the Gospel stories of these days, that is on Monday -- about the withered fig tree, on Tuesday -- about the Last Judgment, on Wednesday -- about the woman who anointed with myrrh and about the conspiracy of Judas with the Jews.

[^583]: The subject of the divine service of Great Friday is the Passion of the Lord, which begins at Vespers, which anticipates Friday. On this day in cathedral temples only one conciliar hierarchal Liturgy is celebrated. And before Vespers (at 9 o'clock) the hierarch consecrates antimensions, at the Liturgy, after "And may the mercies be", -- consecrates chrism, and after the prayer behind the ambo -- washes the feet.

[^588]: In Greek rubrics and in one Slavonic manuscript Triodion which we have, neither censing at any of the 12 Gospels, nor Small Litany is prescribed. Tserkovne Oko prescribes a Small Litany both at the first Gospel and before all five Sessional Hymns, and prescribes leaving the censing at the 8th, 9th, 10th and 11th Gospels. The new Constantinopolitan Typikon prescribes one censing not at the Gospel, but at the beginning of Matins, during the Two Psalms according to the general rubric of Matins. But since among us at Small Matins this censing is omitted, at least here we have given at the first [Gospel] -- censing not only of the holy table, but also of the icons, and choirs, according to the general rubric of the beginning of Matins. Although Greek rubrics at these Gospels do not prescribe censing, nothing strange, for in Greek and Slavonic Typika at Matins Gospels censing is not prescribed. Tserkovne Oko prescribes at the first Gospel two censings: one -- at the beginning, only of the holy table and the whole sanctuary, the second -- at the end: of the whole church, images and choirs. At the six following -- censing of images, the Superior and choirs (however, here it inconsistently agrees with itself, when it is given that at the Sessional Hymns the Priest or deacon censes also the holy table); at Gospels 8, 9, 10 and 11 it does not prescribe censing, and at the 12th again prescribes censing of the whole church, choirs and brethren. The Moscow Typikon follows Tserkovne Oko, however, at the 1st Gospel prescribes only one censing, at the beginning -- of the whole temple; it prescribes inaccurately that the litanies of the Sessional Hymns are said up to the 8th Gospel, for the Sessional Hymns extend only to the 6th Gospel. Although Greek rubrics do not prescribe censing at the Gospels, nevertheless, at the Sessional Hymns they prescribe standing. "We do not sit at such Sessional Hymns, but we sing them standing".

[^600]: The magnificent rite of the Shroud in ancient Triodia and Typika is not given, for it was introduced later; however, today it is used among all followers of the Greek rite, and among us -- also with the exposition of the Holy Mysteries, according to the custom of the Latins of the Austrian State and various German dioceses (Nilles, Calend. T. 2, p. 312). It is described in our Sluzhebnyky, published in Pochaiv back under Stanislaus Augustus in 1767, then in Russian Typika and in the new Typikon of the Patriarchate of Constantinople. However, in our Sluzhebnyky the procession with the Shroud is given only at Vespers, in Russian rubrics -- only at Saturday Matins, after the Great Doxology, and in the Constantinopolitan Typikon the bringing out into the temple to the tomb is prescribed at Vespers, the procession around the temple -- at Matins.
[^601]: Many rubrics add to "The noble Joseph" also the troparion "The angel stood by the tomb" (with the refrain "Glory, Both now"). But Tserkovne Oko, our Manuscript Typikon and the Manuscript Triodion which we have, give only "The noble Joseph", and so they take in the arch-altar temple.
[^602]: According to the rubric of the new Constantinopolitan Typikon, the placing of the Shroud into the tomb takes place during the singing of the Aposticha, in the following way: "The Aposticha are sung, and six priests with uncovered heads, dressed in priestly vestments, go out from the left door of the sanctuary, carrying with reverence on their heads the Epitaphios /Shroud/, of whom the Archimandrite holds also the Holy Gospel, preceded by singers, the Primicerius holding the Divamboulon (a type of candlestick with two lamps), the Deacons with lamps and censers, and thus proceed up to the prepared canopy, and the singers stand in order, singing the Aposticha, and the Deacons censing go around 3 times with the Priests around the canopy. Then they place the Epitaphios inside the canopy, the doorkeeper sprinkles fragrant flowers upon the Epitaphios, and having approached the Patriarch venerates the Epitaphios, blesses the Christians, and ascends the throne. Then the doorkeeper offers him flowers prepared. Then also the holy hierarchs, two by two, venerating the Epitaphios, receive flowers from the Patriarch, likewise also the Ecclesiastical officials. This being done, the 2nd choir sings the Doxastikon, and from the Doxastikon... Now lettest Thou" and the rest. The description which we have from the island of Corfu gives this: "The icon of the Epitaphios is carried on Holy and Great Friday from the sanctuary at the end of Vespers, while the Dismissal Troparia 'The noble Joseph', etc. are sung, and is placed on a prepared table in the middle of the presbyterium, where there are already and remain lit candles with vessels of flowers throughout the whole day until the hour of Matins of Great Saturday (which is usually celebrated on the evening of Great Friday). Where again at the end of the Great Doxology at 'Holy God', the Epitaphios is carried out, but inside the church and, if circumstances permit, -- outside and again is placed on this same table until the time of the Liturgy of Great Saturday, when one priest privately in an epitrachelion places it in the sanctuary in the usual place".

[^605]: In our Pochaiv Triodion nothing is prescribed to cense, it is noted only: "and, having censed crosswise". In the Greek Triodion censing is mentioned only at the 2nd and 3rd stations and it is not mentioned what should be censed. In Tserkovne Oko censing is prescribed at the 1st station of the whole church and brethren according to the order, and at the others -- only of the choirs. In the Constantinopolitan Typikon is prescribed -- only at the 1st station, only of the Shroud and the people: "The Patriarch... censing the Epitaphios, and the whole people".
[^606]: Tserkovne Oko.
[^607]: This troparion is prescribed only once: Typikon of Sabbas, Greek Triodion, Greek Typikon, our Manuscript Typikon, another of Lviv University; other rubrics prescribe it twice, the second time -- with the refrain "Glory, Both now". Tserkovne Oko prescribes it first once, then Glory: the ending, Both now: whole. Obviously, all rubrics have this troparion; and the troparion "The noble Joseph", which is sung before it, is prescribed primarily by various Greek and Slavonic rubrics and the Greek Typikon of Sabbas. The sticheron "Come, let us bless" only our editions have, and the new Constantinopolitan Typikon, before the troparion "The noble Joseph" prescribes also the Resurrection Troparion "When Thou didst descend" and "The angel stood by the tomb". Before the troparion "The noble Joseph" our and Greek rubrics prescribe: "Let us attend. Peace be to all. Wisdom, let us attend", others Slavonic -- only "Wisdom, Aright"; and since they do not prescribe here "The noble Joseph", they prescribe "Wisdom, Aright" to exclaim before the Troparion of the Prophecy. Tserkovne Oko prescribes "Wisdom, Aright" before "The noble Joseph", and before the Troparion of the Prophecy: "Let us attend. Peace to Thee. Wisdom, let us attend". The Entrance, according to the Russian rubric, takes place in the following way: "Then the Superior enters the holy altar with the priests and deacons, vests in all sacred vestments, and the priests -- only in phelonia, comes out with the Gospel under the Shroud, with priests who support, and deacons who cense. At this time ringing is done with all might. He is preceded with candles and with two candlesticks, and both choirs sing the funeral Trisagion. The Abbot, having come before the holy royal doors, stands here, awaiting the conclusion of the last Trisagion. When it ends, the Superior with the Gospel enters the royal doors and places the Gospel on the altar, and the Shroud -- on the prepared table, in the form of a tomb. In monasteries, after the dismissal, the kissing of the Shroud, placed in the tomb, takes place". This is -- the Moscow Typikon. In the Patriarchate of Constantinople it takes place thus: "Great Doxology. Then we begin the sung [Trisagion], preceding the Epitaphios, and going out of the temple, the Entrance takes place, as is customary; as soon as we return, the Patriarch enters directly into the holy sanctuary, with the rest, and immediately exclaims 'Let us attend. Peace be to all. Wisdom'. And the Troparion 'When Thou didst descend' is sung. He censes around the holy table, preceded by the Epitaphios, then 'The angel stood by the tomb' up to 'appeared as a stranger'. After this is sung 'The noble Joseph', up to 'wrapped, laid', and they place the Epitaphios on the holy table. At once the canonarch from outside reads the Troparion, the Prophecy and the Apostle, and the Gospel is said by the Patriarch, in front of the Gate" (New Constantinopolitan Typikon). In various parts of Greece, according to the testimony of Allatius, the procession takes place in the following way: "The custom prevailed, that, while Ps. 118 is sung, and at individual verses individual Troparia are sung, Christ beautifully carved, or skillfully painted on a board, and placed in a bier, with a solemn apparatus of burning candles, Priests, dressed as when they celebrate the sacred solemnities of Masses, the rest of the Clergy accompanying not without order, and the faithful of Christ following the bier through the streets of the city, is carried, and set forth to all to be adored, and kissed: and thus is open to the veneration of all. Meanwhile flowers placed on the image, are sought by all with the greatest zeal, which they promise to themselves for the greatest good, not only of the body, but of domestic affairs" (Nil). Kalend. vol. 2, p. 241).

[^615]: According to the ancient rubric of community life the procession goes from the temple into the narthex through the northern doors of this narthex and there, before its central doors leading into the temple, the beginning of Matins is sung. Carried are: Gospel -- by the Priest and censer -- by the Deacon, preceded by candle-bearers, brethren with lit candles, as you have in the Greek Pentecostarion. To this the Pochaiv Triodion adds the icon of the Resurrection of Christ, and Tserkovne Oko -- also the icon of the Most Holy Theotokos and other holy icons, carried by priests and deacons, so that in such a way the procession would be more majestic, than only with candles. According to the custom of the surroundings of Greece, independent of the Patriarch of Constantinople, before this procession the Bishop or priest, standing in the holy doors with a lit candlestick in hand, exclaims in a loud voice: "Come ye, take light from the unwaning light, and glorify Christ, Who is risen from the dead", that is "Come, receive light from the unwaning light and kiss Christ, risen from the dead". And so all approach one by one, to light their candles from him, forming after this the procession (The Holy Passions. Athens. 1892)
[^616]: In the Greek Triodion this procession is described thus: "About the hour of Matins all the semantrons sound. And the Ecclesiarch distributes candles to the brethren; the Priest with the Deacon vest in all their priestly attire. Then, taking, the Priest the holy Gospel, and the Deacon the censer, and preceded by lamps, we go out to the narthex, holding lit candles, and singing 'Thy Resurrection, O Christ Savior', etc. And in the temple remaining alone the candle-lighter lights all the candles and lamps; and having made a fire, and having put incense into it, places it in the middle of the temple /About the time of Matins all clappers gave notice. The Ecclesiarch distributes candles to the brethren, and the Priest with the Deacon vest in light sacred vestments. Then the Priest, having taken the holy Gospel, and the Deacon -- the censer, preceded by lights, and we all go out to the narthex, holding lit candles and singing: 'Thy Resurrection, O Christ Savior'. In the temple remains only the sacristan, who lights all candles and lamps, after which, having lit a fire, throws incense into it and places in the middle of the temple/."
[^617]: Slavonic rubrics before that prescribe to cense everyone, but we, according to the Greek rubric, cense here only directly the church doors. Evidently also our, or Russian rubrics, according to Tserkovne Oko prescribe for the Priest to sign with the censer three times crosswise the church doors. The Typikon of the Lviv University orders to cense crosswise, but not three times and not the church doors: "Makes a cross with the censer, saying: 'Glory to the Holy'". The Greek Pentecostarion gives only: "and censing says" /and, having censed, exclaims/.
