[^619]: According to the new custom of the Greeks, which Slavs do not accept, before the beginning of Matins the Priest sings the Sunday Gospel of Matins, usually -- the 2nd. This the Greek Typikon of Sabbas does not have, but only newly published Greek Pentecostaria. Also according to the custom (and not according to the church rubric) of the Greeks, independent of the Patriarch of Constantinople, the entrance into the church is accompanied by questions and answers taken from the 23rd Psalm: "Lift up your gates, O ye princes, and the King of Glory shall come in" etc. and when is sung: "The Lord of Hosts, He is the King of Glory", the doors are opened and the entrance into the church takes place... "Especially the custom prevailed to enter through question and answer: Lift up gates, and to open the door only at The Lord of powers, he is the king of glory /Especially the custom prevailed, that the entrance into the church be accompanied by dialogue, question and answer 'Lift up the gates', and the doors are opened only at 'The Lord of Hosts, He is the King of Glory'/, -- is written in the description from Corfu. This custom we meet also among Greek-Melkites, and Italians, and also in various churches of the Latin rite... However, neither in Greek nor in Slavonic rubrics is this met, nor the words of the named psalm fit well here, for according to general explanation they refer not to the descent of Christ into hell, but to His Ascension...
[^620]: "The Priest censes at the beginning of the Canon, according to the order /The Priest censes at the beginning of the canon, as prescribed/ (Greek Triodion).
[^621]: That which is prescribed in Tserkovne Oko and, following it, in our and the Russian Triodia, that the Small Litany after each ode "will be on this holy day outside the sanctuary", does not agree with the Greek Triodion, for in it, instead of "outside the sanctuary", is given "inside the sanctuary",... as have also the Typikon of the Lviv University and the manuscript Slavonic Triodion which we have. However, this contradiction can be eliminated if we say that the Greek Triodion and other rubrics order on this day to sing all litanies for the Priest, and not for the Deacon, and for the Deacon -- only to carry the censer and recite the verses "Let God arise"; and with this assumption the Priest sings all litanies inside the sanctuary, at the holy table... "At each Ode takes place by the Priest, inside the Sanctuary, a Small Litany /At each ode by the Priest, inside the sanctuary, is sung a Small Litany/, -- is written in the Triodion, which also other litanies prescribes to the Priest. Finally, "inside" and "outside", differ only by one letter, therefore we see that copyists could easily make a mistake.
[^622]: According to the rubric of the Greek Triodion the kissing takes place thus: "The Priest takes the holy Gospel, and stands before the doors of the holy Sanctuary but the Superior having come, and having kissed the holy Gospel, and the Priest, receives it from his hands, and stands on the right of the Priest. Then the Brethren all, according to their order, kiss first the holy Gospel, then the Priest and the Superior, and stand also there where they happen to be, and kiss one another /The Priest takes the Holy Gospel and stands before the doors of the sanctuary. And the Abbot, having come and kissed the Gospel and the Priest, takes it from his hands and stands on the right side of the Priest. Then all brethren, according to their rank, kiss first the Gospel, and then -- the Priest and the Abbot, and stand there, where possible, kissing mutually/. According to the rubrics of our Pochaiv, Russian Triodia, Tserkovne Oko and our Manuscript Typikon, the kissing first takes place in the sanctuary between the sacred ministers, then -- in the church, before the iconostasis, between clerics and elders, and at the end -- between the faithful and sacred ministers and between themselves. This is -- the rubric: "The kissing of the Superior with other priests and deacons in the holy altar takes place in this way: He who approaches says: 'Christ is risen', and he answers: 'Truly He is risen' and they kiss. Then the Superior, having taken the cross, stands outside before the holy royal doors, also all priests, as many as there be, and deacons, having taken each the Gospel and holy icons, according to their rank, stand in a row to the right of the Superior. Approach first the most worthy clerics and elders, one by one, and, bowing slightly before the Superior, kiss each the precious cross and Gospel which the Priest and images hold, and the Superior himself on the mouth, saying: 'Christ is risen', and he answers: 'Truly He is risen'. In such a way they kiss also the priests, and they themselves, in order, kiss among themselves, standing in a row to the right of the priests. After them similarly kiss also the faithful" (Moscow Typikon and Pochaiv Triodion 1786).

(On Monday of the Holy Spirit) /Many not considering, also after the Resurrection of our Lord Jesus Christ, read 'O Heavenly King, Comforter' etc., which -- is inadmissible, when our Savior will still be on earth until the first hour of the Ascension, or until the first hour of Pentecost, for at the third hour of this day descended the Holy Spirit... as, finally, from this began to invoke the Holy Spirit the Comforter, from that day, which ceases from the day of the Resurrection until Pentecost (On Monday of the Holy Spirit)/.
[^626]: So about "Christ is risen" in our Sluzhebnyky, except "We have seen", and in its place they have "Christ is risen", however, such is our custom and so in the Pochaiv Triodion of 1786... and in the Moscow Typikon of 1859... Ancient Greek rubrics prescribe "Christ is risen" only instead of "Blessed be the name" and instead of the psalm "I will bless the Lord", as in the Slavonic Typikon of the Lviv University. A later custom of the Greeks -- to sing "Christ is risen" after "Blessed is the Kingdom" three times and, instead of "We have seen the true light" and instead of "Blessed be the name of the Lord", -- three times. However, some of them, after "Blessed is the Kingdom" sing "Christ is risen" with its verses, as is given at the beginning of Resurrection Matins. The Moscow Typikon follows them, but the new Constantinopolitan Typikon does not go. What we said about the custom of the Greeks, we took from a description which we have from the island of Corfu, in which is written the following: "After 'Blessed is the kingdom' the Priest 'Christ is risen', and successively repeat it, first the right followed by the left choir; and this happens on all the days of Pascha until the Ascension. But on the great Sunday, and on those of the New Week we follow to sing it after its verses unchanged; as was said previously at Matins... Is sung successively 'Christ is risen' - as much on the great Sunday as on the remaining days of Pascha at 'With fear' instead of 'We have seen the light', and before the Dismissal three times flowingly instead of 'Blessed be the name', and at the end, at the Dismissal instead of 'Through the prayers' /After 'Blessed is the Kingdom' the Priest: 'Christ is risen', successively again repeat it: first -- the right, then -- and the left choir. And so it will be on all days from the Resurrection to the Ascension. But on the Great Sunday and on the days of Bright Week we continue to sing invariable this with its verses, as is taken at Matins... Successively is sung 'Christ is risen' on the Great Sunday as much as on the rest of the days of the Resurrection: at 'With fear', instead of 'We have seen the light' and before the dismissal three times flowingly, instead of 'Blessed be the name' and at the end, at the dismissal, instead of 'Through the prayers of our holy fathers'/.

[^630]: In the Rite of the Panagia, given in the Horologion before or after the 9th Hour, it is recounted how the apostles after Christ's Resurrection, before the dispersion throughout the whole world, stayed together in Jerusalem, having the custom to dine together and at this time to leave at the table an empty place, on which they placed a pillow, and on it -- : a piece of bread in Christ's portion, that is in memory of Jesus Christ, and after dinner they elevated the piece, saying: "Glory to Thee, O Christ God, help us"; from the Resurrection to the Ascension: "Christ is risen". When the apostles did this after the Dormition of the Most Holy Theotokos, she appeared to them in the air alive, in light radiance, surrounded by angels, saying: "Rejoice, for I am with you all days". And they frightened, instead of "Glory to Thee, O Christ God", exclaimed "All-holy (Panagia) Theotokos, help us". This rite of the Panagia, named so from the name Panagia /All-holy/, by which the apostles invoked then the Most Holy Theotokos, imitating the apostles, was repeated once by the Emperor in the Court... and by people in churches or homes, and predominantly daily in monasteries, as is seen from the service of the meal, given in the Horologion, however, more solemnly -- in Bright Week, in which not a piece of bread, which they ate, but a whole (whole) bread they offered on all days of the week, not eating until Bright Saturday, but only kissing it. And this rite was initially served only at the meal, as it is in the Greek Pentecostarion. The Slavs, for the sake of greater solemnity, did not serve the whole rite only at the meal, but daily, throughout the whole Bright Week, preceded by lights and the icon of the Resurrection carried the Artos from the church to the meal and from the meal to the church, to the sounds of bells, as for Tserkovne Oko has our Pochaiv Triodion and Russian Typika. Today this rite is celebrated among us only in Bright Week and not with all prayers and rites, as the Triodion gives, but only as here, in the text, we gave, however, not only in monasteries, but also in all other churches. The prayers for the blessing and breaking of the Artos the Slavs added to themselves, for in Greek books they are not encountered; the prayer for breaking is not given even in Slavonic rubrics, except ours, but others break it without prayer.

[^737]: Our Menaion and the Tserkovne Oko leave to the decision of the Ecclesiarch to sing to Ven. Onuphrius with Vigil. The Metropolitan Ordinariate -- on 6 with Great Doxology.
[^738]: The Tserkovne Oko prescribes to him only on 6, without Doxology; our manuscript Typikon -- only on 4.
[^739]: Our manuscript Typikon and the Typikon of Lviv University prescribe this service (just as that of August 31) -- only on 6, with Octoechos. The Moscow Typikon and the Greek-Venetian Menaion prescribe the whole service -- only to the Theotokos, however, of the small kind, only at Matins, from the Canon to the end, -- of the large kind; however, the Greek-Venetian Menaion, instead of the regular Katavasia "I will open my mouth," gives the Heirmos of the last Canon and only after the 3rd, 6th and 9th Odes. The Tserkovne Oko and our Menaion prescribe -- with Polyeleos; and our Menaion adds: "if there is no Vigil"; but this we do not do.
[^740]: The Lviv Synod (in the Ukrainian text) appointed the day of memory of these saints on July 5 according to the Gregorian calendar, however, later our ordinariates appointed it on July 5 according to the Julian. St. Athanasius of Athos was transferred from July 5 to July 6 ("Archeparchial News," June 8, 1900).
[^741]: Everything -- according to the rubric of the Theologian, when it falls on the Sunday of the Fathers before Pentecost, with the exception of the Vigil. At the Liturgy: Troparia of all three services -- according to their order. Prokimenon-Alleluia, Apostle-Gospel -- to the Fathers and Vladimir; we do not take the daily ones (Note on p. 296 [→REF:p296]). Communion Hymn -- "Praise" and to Vladimir.
[^742]: Our manuscript Typikon, Greek [Typikon] and [Typikon] of Lviv University and the Tserkovne Oko prescribe the service of St. Anna on 6, together with the [Holy] Women and with the Octoechos, without Doxology, likewise the Moscow Typikon, however, with Doxology. The Greek-Venetian Menaion gives Great Vespers, and Matins -- Great only from the Canon.
[^743]: Troparion or "Alleluia".
[^744]: See July 2, note 1.
[^745]: Typicon S. Sabae; Codex Vatican. An. 1317, sub num. 784; to it corresponds also the one printed in Venice in 1615, Library of St. Augustine in Rome.
[^746]: See note 1 on p. 427 [→REF:p427].
[^747]: Ed. Note. Instead of letters, which in the modern Ukrainian alphabet do not have a direct equivalent, their names in Cyrillic are given.
[^748]: The discrepancy is determined after adding 13 days to the Greek Pascha.
[^749]: M. - March, A. - April, 0 - coincide.
[^750]: Only the Gospel of the 28th Sunday, when it falls before or after the Sunday of the Forefathers, we leave for the Sunday of the Forefathers, and on the 28th -- one of the regular [Gospels] of the Forefathers.
[^751]: I had a student, a Bulgarian, who performed this service on the Holy Mountain [Athos].
[^752]: So holds the Tserkovne Oko in Chapter 7. Finally, now among us the holy doors are high [lattice-work/open], and therefore we do not use a curtain.
[^753]: The translation from Latin was made according to the edition: Ordo Celebrationis vesperarum, matutini et Divinae Liturgiae iuxta recensionem rutenorum, Sacra Congregatio pro Ecclesia Orientali, Roma 1953.
[^754]: Ed. note. In ancient times, "Royal Doors" referred to those doors that led from the narthex to the temple, for at them the Patriarch met the Emperor. Later this name was applied with improper meaning to the middle doors of the iconostasis. In the rubrics of modern Greek liturgical books, "holy doors" are given (see Akolouthia tou Esperinou kai tou Orthrou, Roma 1950, p. 16), therefore we also consistently correct "Royal Doors" to "Holy Doors" everywhere in this Typikon.
[^755]: According to our custom, the holy doors remain open already after the carrying out of the Shroud [Epitaphios].
[^756]: Only one prayer of the current tone should be read throughout the whole week (Lviv Synod, App. XXX, I, p. 392).
[^757]: The Small Litany is usually not taken (see Lviv Synod, App. XXXVI, p. 472).
[^758]: Also -- the cross, if it be behind the throne (see no. 149).
[^759]: He does not make the sign of the cross with the Gospel.
[^760]: Pre-festive days do not introduce any changes into the dismissal. In the Afterfeast, attention should be paid to such changes: 1. The words "resplendent feast" and "light" are omitted. 2. On Wednesday and Friday "cross" is not mentioned: "by the power of the precious and life-giving Cross." 3. If there be a temple of a Feast of the Lord (Nativity, etc.), then outside the feast the usual dismissal is taken, without the mention of the temple feast. 4. On Sunday, the dismissal of the feast is completely left aside and only the Sunday dismissal is taken, and on other days, until the very Apodosis, the dismissal of the feast is taken again. 5. On the Apodosis of the feast, the words "whose feast we give away today" are not added. Likewise on daily dismissals "whose temple it is" or "whose day it is" is omitted, for this is -- rubric explanations (see St. Josaphat, "Rules for Priests," no. 20).
[^761]: If there be readings, see no. 233.
[^762]: Before the Litiya entrance there is no censing of either the throne, or the iconostasis, or the people. It will take place only in the narthex.
[^763]: These gifts are arranged according to such a scheme so that the blessing of the priest depicts upon them the sign of the cross: loaf • wine • • oil • wheat **Chunk 74** **IV. Rubric of Matins in Sundays and Feasts** **1. In Concelebration of One Deacon** **74.** If before this there was no Vigil, then Matins begins thus^[764]: **75.** The priest puts on the *ryasa* the epitrachelion, having previously blessed it, goes before the holy doors and begins: "Blessed is our God." Choir: "Amen," "Glory to Thee, our God, glory to Thee," "O Heavenly King," Trisagion, "Most Holy Trinity," "Our Father." Priest: "For Thine is the kingdom." Choir: "Amen," "Lord, have mercy" (12), "Glory, Both now," "Come, let us worship" (3). The priest enters the sanctuary through the southern doors, recites the Prayer of the Censer, takes the censer, censes the throne from the four sides, the icon behind the altar and other icons of the sanctuary. Then he goes out of the sanctuary through the northern doors, comes before the holy doors and, bowing, censes the icons of the southern part of the iconostasis, beginning from the image of the Savior, the icons of the northern part, beginning from the icon of the Theotokos, then -- the choirs, right and left. He censes the people either from the solea or crossing the whole temple, while the choir reads the 20th(19th) Psalm "The Lord hear thee" and the 21st(20th) "The King shall joy." When the choir begins the Trisagion, the priest returns before the holy doors, censes them and after "Our Father" exclaims: "For Thine is the kingdom," enters the sanctuary through the southern doors, stands before the holy table and, after the completion of the troparia "O Lord, save Thy people," exclaims the Litany for Emperors. After the exclamation "For a merciful," Choir: "Amen," "In the name of the Lord, bless, father." The priest exclaims^[765]: "Glory to the Holy, Consubstantial." Choir: "Amen," "Glory to God in the highest" (3) with small bows and "O Lord, open my lips" (2). The Six Psalms are read. **76.** During the reading of the Six Psalms^[766] the priest, standing before the holy table, begins to recite the Matins Prayers. After the first three psalms, he goes out through the northern doors and, having stood before the holy doors, continues to read the Matins Prayers. After the completion of the psalms, the priest responds to the bow of the deacon and, having returned through the southern doors into the sanctuary, stands before the holy table. At the end of the Six Psalms, the deacon, dressed in the sticharion with the orarion, goes out through the northern doors, pays respect to the priest, stands on his usual place and exclaims the Great Litany. The priest exclaims: "For to Thee belongs." During the singing by the choir of "God is the Lord," the deacon recites the verses and, after a small bow, returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary. **77.** After the Troparia, the reader reads the regular Kathisma, after which the deacon [exclaims] before the holy doors -- the Small Litany, and the priest exclaims: "For Thine is the dominion." Then the reader reads the second regular Kathisma, the deacon -- the second Small Litany, and the priest -- the exclamation "For Thou art a good God." After the Troparia "The Angelic Council," if it is Sunday, or after the Magnification [*Velychannya*], if it is a feast, the deacon again reads the Small Litany, and the priest exclaims: "For blessed." **78.** After the Gradual [*Stepenna*], the holy doors are opened, and the deacon approaches the holy doors and, looking at the people, exclaims: "Let us be attentive." The priest, dressed in the phelonion, blesses the people: "Peace be to all." Deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." The choir sings the Prokimenon. Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." The priest exclaims: "For Holy art Thou, our God." The deacon censes the holy table from the four sides and everything else, according to custom (see no. 33). Choir: "Let everything that has breath praise the Lord." The deacon recites both verses, and the choir repeats: "Let everything that has breath," after which the deacon: "And that we may be vouchsafed." Choir: "Lord, have mercy" (3). The priest takes the Gospel, goes out before the holy doors, stands at a slight distance before them on the solea, places the Gospel on the analogion and reads it, turned to the people. Deacon: "Wisdom, arise, let us hear the Holy Gospel," and the priest blesses: "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Priest: "The reading from the Holy Gospel according to (Name)." Deacon: "Let us be attentive." The priest reads the Matins Gospel. **79.** After the reading, the priest kisses the closed book and carries it to the middle of the temple, where he places it on the tetrapod, and he himself returns through the holy doors into the sanctuary. The deacon reads "Having beheld the Resurrection of Christ," if it is Sunday, or the reader -- the 50th Psalm "Have mercy on me, O God." After the sticheron, the deacon [is] at his usual place: "O God, save Thy people." Choir: "Lord, have mercy" (12) and the priest exclaims: "By the grace and compassions." Choir: "Amen." The Canon begins. The holy doors, if there was no Vigil, are closed. **80.** If there was a Vigil, the priest after the exclamation "By the grace," holding the cross in his hands, goes out through the holy [doors], and the deacon with the oil, blessed at Vespers, and the anointing brush, -- through the northern doors and they stand on the right side of the tetrapod. There the priest anoints crosswise the forehead of everyone who approaches to kiss the Holy Gospel. After the completion of the anointing [*Myrovanne*] they return to the sanctuary: the priest -- through the holy, and the deacon -- through the southern doors and, having closed the holy doors, the priest takes off the phelonion. **81.** After the third and sixth Odes, the deacon sings the Small Litany either before the holy doors, or near the tetrapod, if the anointing was not yet finished, and the priest exclaims the exclamation either from the sanctuary, or from the tetrapod. After the singing of the Katavasia of the eighth Ode, the deacon takes the censer and, having stood before the icon of the Theotokos, says: "The Theotokos and Mother of Light let us magnify in songs" and, having returned through the southern doors into the sanctuary, censes the holy table from four sides and everything else, according to the prescription (see no. 33). After the ninth Ode and after the recitation by the choir of "It is truly meet," if it is not Sunday, but if it is Sunday or a feast, after the singing of the Heirmos, the deacon exclaims from his place the Small Litany. The priest exclaims: "For all the powers of heaven praise Thee." The choir sings the Exaposteilarion. **82.** After the Praises stichera, at "Glory," the deacon opens the holy doors. The priest in the phelonion stands before the throne, the deacon stands to his right and, after the completion of the last sticheron, the priest, turned to the east, exclaims: "Glory to Thee, who hast shown us the Light." The Great Doxology is sung. Then, also according to custom, the Troparion is recited, and the priest, preceded by the deacon, carries the Holy Gospel from the tetrapod into the sanctuary and places it on the holy table. **83.** After this, the deacon stands at his usual place and exclaims the litanies "Have mercy on us, O God" and "Let us complete." The priest blesses the people and exclaims: "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Deacon: "Bow your heads unto the Lord." Choir: "To Thee, O Lord." The priest recites quietly the prayer "O Holy Lord," after which he exclaims: "For Thine it is." The dismissal follows, which the deacon begins: "Wisdom" (see no. 36). **84.** After the dismissal, the reader immediately begins the 1st Hour: "Come, let us worship" (3) and the psalms. After "Our Father," the priest in the epitrachelion: "For Thine is the kingdom." Reader -- Kontakion and "Lord, have mercy" (40). The priest goes out of the sanctuary through the northern doors and before the holy [doors], turned to the east, loudly: "Thou who at all times". Reader: "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Glory, Both now", "More honorable than the Cherubim", "In the name of the Lord, bless, father." Priest: "God be merciful to us." Reader: "Amen." Priest recites the prayer "O Christ, the True Light", "Glory to Thee, O Christ God." Reader: "Glory, Both now", "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Bless." The priest imparts the Small Dismissal, returns into the sanctuary and takes off the epitrachelion. **2. In Concelebration of Two Deacons** **85.** At the end of the Six Psalms, the 1st deacon goes out through the northern doors and exclaims the Great Litany, as well as the verses at "God is the Lord" and, having made a small bow, returns into the sanctuary through the southern doors. After the first Kathisma the 2nd deacon, and after the second Kathisma the 1st deacon, sing the Small Litany. After the Troparia "The Angelic Council" or after the Magnifications, the 2nd deacon likewise sings the Small Litany. After the Gradual [*Stepenna*], the 1st deacon: "Let us be attentive." Priest: "Peace be to all." 2nd deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." 1st deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." Both deacons cense the holy table, the iconostasis, the choirs and the people, as noted in the rubric of Vespers in concelebration with two deacons (see no. 40). At "Let everything that has breath," the 1st deacon recites the first verse, and the 2nd deacon -- the second. **86.** For the anointing of the faithful, the 1st deacon goes out with the priest, and the 2nd exclaims the Small Litany after the third Ode, and also -- after the sixth Ode. After the Katavasia of the eighth Ode, the 1st deacon takes the censer, goes out through the northern doors, stands before the icon of the Theotokos and calls: "The Theotokos and Mother of Light," then returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary and, together with the 2nd deacon, censes the throne and everything else, as noted above (see no. 39), and after the censing they return into the sanctuary: the 1st deacon -- through the southern, and the 2nd -- through the northern doors. After the ninth Ode, the 1st deacon exclaims the Small Litany. **87.** After the Praises stichera, the holy doors are opened. The 1st deacon stands before the holy table to the right of the priest, and the 2nd -- to the left. After the Great Doxology, all, having made a small bow, go to the tetrapod, the priest takes the Holy Gospel and, preceded by the deacons, returns into the sanctuary. **88.** After this, the deacons go out: the 1st deacon exclaims the first litany "Have mercy on us, O God," and the 2nd -- the second "Let us complete." 1st deacon: "Bow your heads unto the Lord." The dismissal follows, which the 1st deacon begins: "Wisdom" (see no. 36, note). **3. Without a Deacon** **89.** A priest who serves Matins without a deacon does and says everything that belongs to the deacon, considering this: **90.** After the completion of the Six Psalms, he does not return into the sanctuary, but, standing before the holy doors, exclaims the Great Litany and its exclamation: "For to Thee belongs," as well as the verses during the singing by the choir of "God is the Lord." After the completion of this, he makes a small bow and returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary. It should be noted that when the priest does not have enough time to recite all the Matins Prayers before the iconostasis, he may finish them in the sanctuary during the reading of the Kathismata. After the Prokimenon, he himself exclaims: "Let us pray to the Lord"; reads the verses at "Let everything that has breath"; before the reading of the Gospel, exclaims: "Let us be attentive," and after the Gospel reads "Having beheld the Resurrection of Christ." After the 3rd and 6th Odes of the Canon -- Small Litanies and exclaims from the throne or from the place where he anoints. After the anointing, he returns through the holy doors into the sanctuary and takes off the phelonion. **91.** After the Katavasia of the 8th Ode, he goes out in the epitrachelion through the northern doors, stands before the icon of the Theotokos and calls: "The Theotokos and Mother of Light," then censes, as noted above (see no. 33). After the censing, he returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary, exclaims the Small Litany and its exclamation. **92.** After the Praises stichera, at "Glory," he puts on the phelonion, opens the holy doors and, after the last sticheron, exclaims: "Glory to Thee, who hast shown us the Light." Everything else takes place as was presented (see nos. 82-83). **93.** After the dismissal, the priest closes the holy doors, takes off the phelonion and the 1st Hour begins. **4. In Concelebration of Priests** **94.** Concelebrants, in an even number, put on epitrachelia over their *ryasas* and put on phelons during the reading of the Kathisma and stand on the sides of the holy table, as at Vespers (see no. 50). During the singing of the Polyeleos, all go out, having made a small bow, through the holy doors, having lowered the phelonion and hands down, in front -- the younger ones. Two first ones carry the icon of the feast or saint, if it has not yet been placed on the left side of the tetrapod between both choirs, and place it on the tetrapod; all stand on the sides of the tetrapod in two rows, facing one another, the principal celebrant stands in the middle before the tetrapod, and to his right -- the deacon. **

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

Diagram: At the Magnification** [Left Column] Candle-bearer ... 6 ... 4 ... 2 ... Concelebrants [Center] TETRAPOD [Right Column] Candle-bearer ... 5 ... 3 ... 1 ... Concelebrants [Bottom] Celebrant ... Deacon **95.** Then all sing the Magnification. When the choir repeats the Magnification, the priest, preceded by the deacon with a lighted candle, censes from four sides the icon of the feast or saint on the tetrapod, the holy table, the sanctuary, the iconostasis, the concelebrants, both choirs, the people and once more the icon of the feast, but only from the front. If, however, the usual censing takes place before the Gospel, then at the Magnification the priest censes only the icon itself. Choir: "Glory" and again the Magnification. Then the celebrant and concelebrants sing the Magnification once more. **96.** After the Magnifications all, the younger ones -- in front, return through the holy doors into the sanctuary before the holy table. After the Gospel all, having made a small bow, depart and take off their vestments. **Shortening of Matins**^[767] **1. Beginning** -- The priest, having put on the epitrachelion, censes as usual (see at "Lord, I have cried," no. 75). -- Then he exclaims: "Glory to the Holy," and the choir recites everything else and the 142nd Psalm on Sunday or the regular one -- on feasts. -- After the Great Litany -- "God is the Lord," Troparion of the Sunday or Feast, Theotokion according to the tone of the Troparion. **2. Sung Kathismata** -- Regular Kathismata with Sessional Hymns are not taken, but sung ones are taken thus: "The Angelic Council" -- only on Sundays, "Praise the name of the Lord" (Polyeleos) -- only on feasts, "By the waters of Babylon" -- only on the Sundays of Great Lent. -- The priest at the appointed time puts on the phelonion, opens the holy doors and exclaims: "Peace be to all." Then he censes. If there was censing at the Magnification, then before the Reading of the Gospel there will be no censing. -- Prokimenon, "Let everything that has breath" -- according to the tone of the season. **3. Bringing out the Gospel** -- The priest, having read the Gospel, carries the Holy Book out to the tetrapod, accompanied by two candle-bearers. -- The Reader, if there is no deacon, reads "Having beheld the Resurrection of Christ." -- All go to kiss the Gospel. If there was a *Litiya*, then the anointing takes place (see no. 80). -- Having returned to the throne, the priest recites the prayer "O God, save." After this he does not close the holy doors in view of the shortening of Matins. **4. Magnification of the Theotokos** -- Having recited the prayer "O God, save," the priest takes the censer and goes out before the icon of the Theotokos. -- There he exclaims: "The Theotokos and Mother of Light," censes the icon, then returns into the sanctuary and censes everything, as usual. -- The choir sings "More honorable than the Cherubim" at the beginning and at the end of the verses, which both choirs recite alternately. **5. Laudatory Prayers** -- Psalms 148, 149 and 150 are sung singly, in turn. -- After "Most Blessed" the priest exclaims: "Glory to Thee, who hast shown us the Light." At the Great Doxology there will be no censing. -- During the singing of the Troparion, the priest carries the Gospel back, and after the completion -- immediately says the dismissal. **Beginning of Paschal Matins** At Paschal Matins the censing takes place with special solemnity. The servers, having put on the best vestments, as at the Divine Liturgy, go out before the throne in the usual order and make a bow all together. The principal celebrant gives the Gospel to the 1st server, and to the 2nd -- the icon of the Resurrection of Christ, he himself takes the cross with his left hand, and with the right (from the deacon) -- the censer. He censes first the throne, and afterwards -- the servers. Then the principal celebrant, having given the censer to the deacon, stands at his place. All bow before the throne and turn to the east to go out to the narthex. The exit takes place according to the usual order of seniority under the peeling of bells and with the singing of the hymn "Thy Resurrection, O Christ Savior." And the order is such: candle-bearers, priests, deacons with lighted candles, and behind them -- the principal celebrant. All are also given lighted candles. In the narthex all stand before the closed church doors, as in the 

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

diagram below: **Church doors** **___________I_______I__________** **Left Kliros** ...................................... **Right Kliros** **A2** ..................................................... **A1** **C4** ..................................................... **C3** **C2** ..................................................... **C1** **D2** **PC** **D1** **People** Here the principal celebrant takes the censer from the deacon and censes the icons of the narthex, the kliroses and the people. The deacon precedes him the entire time with a lighted candle. Then the principal celebrant returns before the doors and censes the deacon; and then the latter, having taken the censer from the principal celebrant, censes him and immediately gives the censer back to the principal celebrant, who thrice censes the doors and then exclaims: "Glory to the Holy." After "Amen," the principal celebrant with the concelebrants sings thrice "Christ is risen" and the verses "Let God arise," to which the people respond with the song "Christ is risen." After the last "Christ is risen," the principal celebrant opens the doors (Among us he knocks thrice with the cross) and enters the church, and behind him all the servers and people (see no. 71; Liturgicon, pp. 141-146).
[^764]: The initial part "for the emperors" we do not take, we omit. At Matins in the shortened form, the priest, having censed according to the rubric, exclaims before the holy doors: "Glory to the Holy" and remains there to recite the Matins Prayers. There will be no censing during the reading of the psalms. Generally censing takes place thus: -- there will be no censing at Daily Matins and when Great Matins follows immediately after a Vigil; -- if Matins is celebrated separately, the priest or deacon censes as usual (see Liturgicon, Rome 1952, pp. 52, 88, 130).
[^765]: From here Matins in the shortened form begins.
[^766]: The Lviv Synod established such an order of recitation: "From the Six Psalms, only one psalm should be read in turn daily, namely: on Monday -- the first in order, on Tuesday -- the second, on Wednesday -- the third, on Thursday -- the fourth, on Friday -- the fifth, on Saturday -- the sixth, on Sunday -- again the sixth" (App. no. XXX, IV. Matins, p. 393).
[^767]: Such a shortening is generally practiced, therefore we present it here as an appendix. **Chunk 75** **V. Rubric of the Divine Liturgy** **of St. John Chrysostom and St. Basil the Great** **1. In Concelebration of One Deacon** **97.** According to the ancient custom of the Eastern Church, only one Holy Liturgy may be celebrated at the same holy table. However, one may depart from this rule if the Divine Liturgy must be repeated for the benefit of the faithful. If there is one or several secondary churches in the parish, then the more solemn Liturgy is celebrated in the main sanctuary, and other liturgies should be celebrated rather in the side sanctuaries. **98.** The Eucharistic bread does not absolutely have to be baked on the day the Holy Sacrifice is offered. The same bread can be kept for several days and used at several liturgies, provided that all the ceremonies of the Proskomedia are observed over it or over a part of it, cutting the bread and removing the Lamb and particles according to the prescription. Also, it is not necessary to always use five prosphora, if the Lamb and all particles can be taken from one and the same prosphora. The custom of using five prosphora may be kept, if one pleases, when celebrating more solemn liturgies (see no. 179). **99.** The priest who wishes to serve the Sacrament must first of all be reconciled with all and hold nothing against anyone, keep his heart as far as possible from evil thoughts, be continent already from the evening and keep the fast until the very time of the service and prepare himself for the offering of the sacrifice by prayers (see no. 190). **100.** At the prescribed time, the priest enters the church and, together with the deacon, bows three times before the holy doors to the east. Then the deacon says in a low voice: "Bless, Master." Priest: "Blessed is our God." Deacon: "Amen." And the deacon begins to say: "Glory to Thee, our God," "O Heavenly King," "Holy God" (3), "Glory, Both now," "Most Holy Trinity," "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Glory, Both now," "Our Father." Priest: "For Thine is the kingdom." Deacon: "Amen." Then they recite together: "Have mercy on us, O Lord, have mercy on us," Glory: "Lord, have mercy on us," Both now: "The door of compassion." They approach the icon of the Savior, venerate it with a small bow and, kissing it, say: "We worship Thine immaculate Icon." Having bowed before the holy doors, in the same manner they venerate and kiss the icon of the Theotokos, saying the troparion "Forasmuch as thou art a well-spring of compassion." **101.** After this the priest and deacon return before the holy doors, and the priest, bowing his head, recites the prayer "O Lord, stretch forth Thy hand." Then the priest and deacon bow also to the right and left choirs and go into the sanctuary: the priest -- through the southern, and the deacon -- through the northern doors, saying: "I will enter into Thy house" (see no. 178). **102.** Having entered the sanctuary, they make three small bows before the holy table and kiss: the priest -- the Holy Gospel, and the deacon -- the holy table and, if there exists a custom, both -- the altar cross. Having arrived at the place where the sacred vestments are kept, each takes his sticharion in his hands and makes three small bows to the east, saying to himself: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner." **103.** Then the deacon approaches the priest and, holding in his right hand the sticharion with the orarion and cuffs and bowing his head, says: "Bless, Master, the sticharion with the orarion." And the priest blesses, saying: "Blessed is our God." Deacon: "Amen." **104.** Then the deacon withdraws and, at some place in the sanctuary, puts on the sticharion, praying thus: "My soul shall rejoice in the Lord." Having kissed the orarion, he places it on his left shoulder. Putting the cuff on the right hand, he says: "Thy right hand, O Lord," and on the left: "Thy hands have made me." After this he goes to the table of oblation, unfolds the antimension [*iliton*], places the diskos on the left side, and the chalice -- on the right, and prepares also the spear, star-cover, veils and purificators for the holy offering of the sacrifice. **105.** The priest, in the right part of the sanctuary, vests thus: having taken the sticharion in his left hand, he makes three small bows to the east, as was said about this, and, blessing it, says: "Blessed is our God." Then he puts it on, saying: "My soul shall rejoice in the Lord." Having taken the epitrachelion and blessed it, he puts it on himself and says: "Blessed is God, Who pours out His grace." Having taken the zone [belt], he girds himself, saying: "Blessed is God, Who girds me with strength." Putting the cuff on the right hand, he says: "Thy right hand, O Lord," and on the left: "Thy hands have made me." Then he takes the epigonation [*nabedrenyk*], if he has one, and, having blessed and kissed it, hangs it over his right knee, saying: "Gird Thy sword." After this, having taken and blessed the phelonion, he kisses it and says: "Thy priests, O Lord." **106.** One may vest also in the sacristy. **107.** Dressed thus in vestments, the priest and deacon go to the table of oblation, where they wash their hands, saying: "I will wash my hands among the innocent." **108.** Then they make three small bows before the table of oblation and say: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner," "Thou hast redeemed us." The deacon says: "Bless, Master," and the priest begins: "Blessed is our God." Deacon: "Amen." After this the priest takes a prosphora with his left hand, and with his right -- the holy spear, makes with it the sign of the cross three times over the seal of the prosphora and says thrice: "In remembrance of our Lord and God," immediately thrusts the spear into the right side of the seal, cuts and says: "As a sheep led to the slaughter," and into the left: "And as a blameless lamb," into the upper side of the seal: "In His humiliation," into the lower: "And who shall declare His generation." And the deacon, observing piously this mystery, says each time: "Let us pray to the Lord," holding the orarion with his right hand. Then he says: "Take up, Master." The priest, having thrust the holy spear obliquely into the right side of the prosphora, lifts out the holy bread and says: "For His life is taken away from the earth" and, having placed it face up on the holy diskos, after the call of the deacon: "Sacrifice, Master," cuts it crosswise and says: "Sacrificed is the Lamb of God" and turns the other side of the bread, which has the cross, upwards. The deacon says: "Pierce, Master." The priest pierces the holy bread with the spear in the upper right corner, where the letters "IC" are imprinted, saying: "One of the soldiers." 

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

[Diagram of the Lamb] NI KA IC XC **109.** The deacon, having taken wine and water, says to the priest: "Bless, Master, the holy union" and, when he has blessed, the deacon himself or the priest pours wine and a little water into the holy chalice, according to established prescriptions. **110.** Then the priest takes the second prosphora in his hands, however if there is no second or other prosphora, he finishes the prescribed liturgical actions on one, saying: "In honor and memory" and, having taken a particle, places it to the right of the holy bread, near its middle, saying: "At Thy right hand stood the Queen." **111.** Then, having taken the third prosphora, he says: "Of the honorable, heavenly," takes the first particle, places it to the left of the holy bread, beginning the first row. Then he says: "Of the honorable, glorious Prophet, Forerunner." The taken particle he places under the first and says: "Of the holy, glorious," and then places the third particle under the second, finishing the first row. Then he says: "Of our holy Fathers"; having taken the fourth particle, he places it next to the first, beginning the second row. Then he says: "Of the holy Apostle, Protomartyr" and, having taken the fifth particle, places it under the first [of the second row], with which he begins the second row. After this he says: "Of our venerable and God-bearing [Fathers]" and, having taken the sixth particle, places it under the second [of the second row], finishing the second row. Then he says: "Of the holy and wonderworking Unmercenaries." Having taken the seventh particle, he places it next to the first [of the second row], beginning the third row. Then again he says: "Of the holy and righteous Ancestors of God" and places the eighth particle under the first [of the third row]. He takes the ninth particle, saying: "Of Saint (Name) and all saints," and places it at the end of the third row, finishing it. **112.** After this he takes the fourth prosphora and says: "Remember, O Master, Lover of mankind, our most holy [Pontiff]," and places the taken particle below the holy bread. Then he mentions by name the living, whom he wishes, and for each name takes out a particle, saying: "Remember, O Lord, (Name)." **113.** Finally he takes the fifth prosphora, mentions the bishop who ordained him, and by name the deceased, whom he wishes. For each name he takes out a particle, saying: "Remember, O Lord, the soul." Then he says: "And of all in the hope of resurrection" and takes out a particle. After this he says: "Remember, O Lord, according to the multitude of Thy compassions" and takes out a particle. It should be noted that one may add other particles for the living and the deceased until the Great Entrance itself (see no. 192). **114.** He gathers the particles on the diskos under the holy bread, so that they be together and so that none falls off^[768]. **115.** The deacon takes the censer and, having put in incense, says to the priest: "Bless, Master, the incense" and immediately says himself: "Let us pray to the Lord," and the priest blesses and recites the Prayer of the Censer "Incense we offer to Thee" (see no. 20). Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." The priest, having censed the star-cover, places it over the holy bread, saying: "And the star came." Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." The priest, having censed likewise the first veil, covers with it the holy bread with the diskos and says: "The Lord reigns." Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord. Cover, Master." The priest, having censed likewise the second veil, covers with it the holy chalice, saying: "Thy virtue." Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord. Cover, Master." The priest, having censed in the same manner the third veil, the so-called *aer* [vozdukh], covers with it the diskos and chalice, saying: "Cover us with the shelter." Then the priest, having taken the censer, censes the table of oblation, bowing together with the deacon, and says: "Blessed is our God," and the deacon responds: "Always, now and ever." The priest gives the censer to the deacon either now, or after the Prayer of the Offering. **116.** Then the deacon says: "For the precious gifts offered," and the priest, making no sign of blessing, recites the Prayer of the Offering: "O God, our God," after which he makes the dismissal there, speaking thus: "Glory to Thee, O Christ God." Deacon: "Glory, Both now," "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Bless." On Sunday the priest says the dismissal thus: "Christ, Who rose from the dead," and on other days: "Christ, our true God." Deacon: "Amen." **117.** After the dismissal of the Proskomedia, the priest goes before the holy table, and the deacon censes the table of oblation three times, then the holy table from the four sides, saying quietly: "In the tomb" and the 50th(51st) Psalm, after which he censes the icon behind the altar. He goes out of the sanctuary through the northern doors, comes before the holy doors and, having bowed before them, censes the icons of the southern part of the iconostasis, beginning from the icon of the Savior, then -- the icons of the northern part, beginning from the icon of the Theotokos, and then -- the choirs, right and left. He censes the faithful either from the solea, or, if there is a custom, going through the church to the very narthex. Having returned through the southern doors into the sanctuary, he censes the holy table once more, only from the front, and likewise -- the celebrant (see nos. 9, 20, 33, 39, 54; also no. 177). **118.** Then he gives the censer to the server, and himself stands to the right of the priest. Standing together before the holy table, they recite "O Heavenly King." Then they bow three times, saying: "Glory to God in the highest" (2), "O Lord, open my lips," then they kiss: the priest -- the Holy Gospel, and the deacon -- the holy table (see no. 102). After this the deacon bows his head before the priest and, holding the orarion with three fingers of his right hand, says: "It is time." The priest signs him and says: "Blessed is our God," and the deacon: "Pray for me, Master." Priest: "May the Lord direct thy steps." And again the deacon: "Remember me, holy Master." Priest: "May the Lord God remember thee." Deacon: "Amen." The deacon, having made a small bow and holding the orarion with three fingers of his right hand, goes out through the northern doors, for the holy doors remain closed until the Entrance itself and, having stood at his place before the holy doors, makes piously three small bows and prays quietly: "O Lord, open my lips." After this, he raises the end of the orarion with his right hand and exclaims: "Bless, Master." **119.** And the priest, standing in the middle before the holy table and making the sign of the cross over it with the Holy Gospel^[769], begins loudly: "Blessed is the kingdom." Choir: "Amen." The deacon sings the Great Litany "In peace let us pray to the Lord," and the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the First Antiphon "O Lord our God." Exclamation: "For to Thee belongs." Choir: "Amen." The First Antiphon or the First Typika Psalm is sung, and the deacon, having made a small bow, departs from his place and stands before the icon of Christ, holding the orarion with three fingers of his right hand. **120.** After the completion of the Antiphon, the deacon returns to his place and, having made a small bow, exclaims: "Again and again." And the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Second Antiphon: "O Lord our God, save Thy people." Exclamation: "For Thine is the dominion." Choir: "Amen." Likewise the Second Antiphon or Typika [Psalm] is sung. The deacon does the same as at the first prayer, only he stands now before the icon of the Theotokos. After the Antiphon the choir sings: "Glory, Both now," "Only-begotten Son," and the priest says nothing and at "became man" does not bow. **121.** Then the deacon, having returned again to the usual place, sings: "Again and again," and the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Third Antiphon "Thou who hast given us." Exclamation: "For Thou art a good." Choir: "Amen." The deacon returns into the sanctuary through the southern doors. Here the holy doors are opened. **122.** The Third Antiphon or the Beatitudes, if it is Sunday, is sung. When the singers reach "Glory," the priest and deacon, standing before the holy table, make three small bows. Then the priest takes the Holy Gospel, gives it to the deacon and lowers the phelonion. Both go around the holy table from the right side and, having gone out through the northern doors, preceded by candle-bearers, make the Little Entrance. Having come before the holy doors, the candle-bearers stand on opposite sides: one -- near the icon of the Theotokos, and the other -- of the Savior, the priest -- in the middle, and the deacon -- slightly in front of him, to the right. Both bow their heads and the deacon says in a low voice: "Let us pray to the Lord," and the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Entrance "O Master, Lord our God." After the completion of the prayer, the deacon says in a low voice to the priest, holding the orarion with three fingers and pointing to the east: "Bless, Master, the holy entrance." The priest blesses to the east and says: "Blessed is the entrance." Then the deacon presents to the priest the Holy Gospel for kissing. When the last verse of the Antiphon or Beatitudes is finished, the deacon goes out to the center, stands before the priest, raises his hands slightly and, showing the Holy Gospel^[770], exclaims: "Wisdom, arise." Then they enter the sanctuary and the deacon places the Holy Gospel on the throne, and the candle-bearers, having bowed together before the holy doors, return to their places. The choir sings: "Come, let us worship," "Save us... who art wonderful in the saints...", and if it is Sunday: "Save us... who rose from the dead...". After this -- the usual troparia. **123.** The priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Trisagion "O Holy God." When the singers reach the last troparion, the deacon bows his head before the priest and, holding the orarion with three fingers in his hand, says: "Bless, Master, the time of the Thrice-Holy," and the priest blesses him and exclaims: "For Holy art Thou, our God." The deacon withdraws to the holy doors and, turned to the people, with the end of the orarion raised by three fingers of the right hand, exclaims: "and unto ages of ages." Choir: "Amen." During the singing of the Trisagion, the priest and deacon also recite it, making simultaneously three small bows before the holy table. **124.** Then the deacon says to the priest: "Command, Master" and departs to the High Place. The priest, going, says: "Blessed is he that comes." Deacon: "Bless, Master," and the priest: "Blessed art Thou on the throne" and blesses the High Place. It is known that the priest should not go up to the High Place, nor sit on it. It befits him to sit on the southern side of the High Throne. **125.** After the completion of the Trisagion, the deacon approaches the holy doors and, holding the orarion with three fingers of the raised right hand, says: "Let us be attentive," and the priest blesses the people and exclaims: "Peace be to all." Then again the deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive" and returns to the priest. The choir sings the Prokimenon, the Psalm of David. After the Prokimenon, the deacon: "Wisdom," and the reader, dressed in a sticharion, in the middle of the sanctuary [temple], before the solea, reads the title of the Apostle: "The Acts...". And again the deacon: "Let us be attentive." After the completion of the reading of the Apostle, the priest says: "Peace be to thee." Deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." The choir sings "Alleluia" with verses. **126.** During the singing of "Alleluia," the deacon, having taken the censer and put incense into it, approaches the priest and says: "Bless, Master, the incense." Having received the blessing from the priest, who says: "Blessed is our God," he censes around the holy table, the whole sanctuary, the priest, the icons of the sanctuary, the icons of the iconostasis, both choirs and the people (see nos. 33 and 75). And the priest, standing before the holy table, recites quietly the Prayer before the Gospel "Illumine our hearts." The deacon, having given away the censer, approaches the priest and, having bowed his head before him and holding the orarion with his fingers, points to the Holy Gospel and says loudly: "Bless, Master, the proclaimer of the holy Apostle." The priest, blessing him, exclaims: "May God, through the prayers," and gives him the Holy Gospel, and the deacon answers: "Amen" and, having bowed to the Holy Gospel, takes it, goes out through the holy doors, preceded by candle-bearers who go out through the side doors, stands on the ambo or not far from the holy doors at the designated place, there places the Holy Gospel on the analogion and reads it, turned to the people. The priest stands before the throne and, looking to the west, exclaims: "Wisdom, arise, let us hear the Holy Gospel." Then he blesses: "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Deacon: "The reading from the Holy Gospel according to (Name)." Choir: "Glory to Thee, O Lord, glory to Thee." Priest: "Let us be attentive." After the reading of the Gospel, the priest says to the deacon: "Peace be to thee who proclaimest." Choir: "Glory to Thee, O Lord, glory to Thee." The deacon comes to the very holy doors and gives the rolled Holy Gospel to the priest^[771], who kisses it and places it in the middle of the throne before the tabernacle or places it on the right side of the holy table; the holy doors are closed again. **127.** The deacon stands at the usual place and begins thus: "Let us all say." The priest recites quietly the Prayer "O Lord our God." Exclamation: "For a merciful." Choir: "Amen." Then the deacon: "Pray, ye catechumens." The priest quietly recites the Prayer for the Catechumens "O Lord our God." Exclamation: "That with us they also." Choir: "Amen." The priest unfolds the antimension [*iliton*]. The deacon says loudly: "All catechumens, depart; catechumens, depart; all catechumens, depart. Let no catechumen remain. Only the faithful." **128.** The priest recites quietly the First Prayer of the Faithful "We thank Thee." Deacon: "Help us, save us, have mercy." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." Deacon: "Wisdom." Exclamation: "For to Thee belongs." Choir: "Amen." Deacon: "Again and again." The priest recites quietly the Second Prayer of the Faithful "Again and oftentimes." Deacon: "Help us, save us, have mercy." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." Deacon: "Wisdom" and enters the sanctuary through the northern doors^[772]. The priest, not turning to the people, exclaims: "That being kept under Thy dominion." Choir: "Amen"; and the holy doors are opened. **129.** During the singing of the Cherubic Hymn, the deacon, having taken the censer and put incense into it, approaches the priest, saying: "Bless, Master, the incense" and, having received the blessing: "Blessed is God," recites the 50th(51st) Psalm and censes around the holy table, the icon behind the altar, the icons of the iconostasis, both choirs and the people. At the end, having returned through the southern doors into the sanctuary, he censes the priest^[773]. The priest, having lifted his hands up, recites quietly the prayer "No one is worthy." After the censing, the deacon stands to the right of the priest, holding the censer on the ring finger of his left hand. The priest together with the deacon, having lifted their hands up, recite the Cherubic Hymn three times, each time making a small bow. After this, where there exists a custom, the priest and deacon kiss the holy table and, if they wish, the altar cross; then they go, the deacon -- in front, directly to the side altar. There the priest, having taken the censer, censes the Holy Gifts crosswise, praying quietly: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner," gives the censer to the deacon, who holds it on one of the fingers of his right hand. The deacon says to the priest: "Take up, Master," and the priest takes the large veil, which is called the *aer*, and places it on the deacon's left shoulder, saying: "Lift up your hands." Then he takes the holy diskos, covered with the small veil, and places it with attentiveness and piety on the deacon's head^[774], and the deacon, holding the end of the orarion with his left hand, holds the diskos with both hands on his head. The priest himself takes the chalice, covered with the small veil, and holds it before him. Both go out through the northern doors, preceded by candle-bearers. These last arrive at the very holy doors and stand on both sides of them. The deacon, going out, calls: "All of you, Orthodox Christians" and enters through the holy doors into the sanctuary, where he waits for the priest on the right side. The priest exclaims: "Our most holy [Pontiff]" and before the holy doors, when he exclaims "And all of you, Orthodox Christians," he turns to the people^[775]; then he enters the sanctuary.
[^768]: If a larger number of communicants is expected, then the priest places a larger number of particles on the diskos, and on them places the Lamb (see no. 230).
[^769]: He holds the book vertically.
[^770]: He does not make the sign of the cross with the book, but only lifts it up.
[^771]: After the reading, neither the deacon nor the priest blesses the people with the holy book.
[^772]: This part is shortened thus: Deacon: "Only the faithful, again and again in peace let us pray to the Lord." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." The priest reads the Second Prayer of the Faithful, for the first is very similar in content to the prayer "No one is worthy."
[^773]: This time the table of oblation is not censed, for it will be censed later, before the Great Entrance (see nos. 9, 20, 149, 157).
[^774]: The shape of current diskoses does not allow fulfilling this requirement, therefore the deacon holds the diskos in his hands.
[^775]: The priest does not bless the people with the chalice, for there are no consecrated Gifts in it yet (see St. Josaphat, "Rules for Priests," S. Josaphat Hieromartyr; Documenta Beatifications et canonizations, I, 235. Lviv Synod, "Appendix", 1897, § IV, "Holy Liturgy," p. 217). **Chunk 76** **130.** The priest, having entered through the holy doors, places the holy chalice on the throne; he also takes from the deacon^[776] the holy diskos and places it on the throne, to the left of the chalice. Having removed the small veils from the diskos and chalice, he places them on the throne, and with the large veil, that is the *aer*, which he takes from the deacon's shoulder and censes over the censer, he covers the Holy Gifts, saying: "The noble Joseph." Then, having taken the censer from the deacon's hands, he censes the Holy Gifts crosswise, saying: "Do good, O Lord" (see nos. 9, 20, 149). During this prayer the holy doors are closed, and the candle-bearers, having made together a bow before the holy doors, withdraw to their places. **131.** Having given away the censer, the priest lowers the phelonion and, bowing his head, says to the deacon: "Remember me, brother and concelebrant," and the deacon responds to him: "May the Lord God remember thy priesthood." Priest to this: "Pray for me, my concelebrant." The deacon, bowing his head, holding the orarion with three fingers of his right hand, says to the priest: "The Holy Spirit shall come upon thee." Priest: "And the power of the Most High." Then the deacon to him: "Remember me, holy Master." Priest: "May the Lord God remember thee." Deacon: "Amen." **132.** The deacon, having bowed to the priest, goes out through the northern doors and, standing at the usual place, says: "Let us complete." The priest reads quietly the Prayer of the Offering, after the placing of the divine gifts on the holy table "O Lord God Almighty." Exclamation: "Through the compassions." Choir: "Amen." The priest turns to the people and blesses: "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Deacon: "Let us love one another," and the priest bows three times, saying quietly: "I will love Thee, O Lord" and kisses the Holy Gifts as they are covered: first -- the holy diskos, then -- the holy chalice, and finally -- the edge of the holy table before himself. The deacon, having made three small bows at his place and having kissed his orarion where the sign of the cross is on it, exclaims: "The doors, the doors" (see no. 200). The priest lifts the large veil, that is the *aer*, and, holding it over the Holy Gifts, recites together with the people the Symbol of Faith "I believe in one God" and does not bow at the words "and became man"^[777]; having kissed the *aer*, he places it on the usual (one) place on the throne. **133.** Deacon: "Let us stand well." Choir: "A mercy of peace." The deacon, having made a small bow, enters through the southern doors into the sanctuary, stands to the right of the priest and, if necessary, takes the fan [*rypida*] and fans with it piously over the Holy Gifts. If there is no fan -- he does this with the small (folded) veil. The priest at the words "The grace of our Lord" blesses the people. Choir: "And with thy spirit." The priest, having turned to the east, lifts his hands up and calls: "Let us lift up our hearts." Choir: "We lift them up unto the Lord." Then the priest, folding his hands on his chest and bowing before the holy table, says: "Let us give thanks unto the Lord." Choir: "It is meet and right," and the priest recites quietly the prayer "It is meet and right to hymn Thee." Exclamation: "Singing the triumphant hymn." Then the deacon approaches the priest from the left side and, having taken the holy star-cover with his right hand, strikes the holy diskos with it above, below, on the left and on the right side, making thus the sign of the holy cross over it, and, having kissed the star-cover, places it on the holy table. When the choir sings "Holy, Holy, Holy," the priest does not make the sign of the holy cross on himself with the star-cover. **134.** After this the deacon stands to the right of the priest and, if necessary, takes into his hands the fan or small veil and silently, with all attention and reverence, fans over the Holy Gifts. The priest recites quietly the prayer "With these blessed powers, O Master, Lover of mankind." At the words "took bread in His holy and most pure, and blameless hands, gave thanks and blessed," he does not take the holy diskos into his hands and does not lift it, but only blesses it once. Then, bowing his head and pointing with his hand to the holy diskos (the deacon does the same with the orarion), he exclaims: "Take, eat." Choir: "Amen." The priest together with the deacon bow low, making the sign of the holy cross. The priest says quietly: "Likewise also the chalice" and again blesses once. After this, bowing his head and pointing with his hand to the holy chalice (the deacon does the same with the orarion), he exclaims: "Drink of it, all of you." Choir: "Amen." Again the priest and deacon bow low, simultaneously making the sign of the holy cross on themselves. **135.** The priest recites quietly the prayer "Remembering this," and the deacon, crossing his hands, taking with the right -- the holy diskos, and with the left lifting slightly the holy chalice, makes the sign of the cross over the antimension [*iliton*]. The priest exclaims: "Thine own of Thine own." Choir: "We praise Thee, we bless Thee." And again the priest and deacon make a small bow. Then the priest recites quietly the prayer "Again we offer unto Thee this reasonable." The deacon lays aside the fan or veil, approaches the priest and both make three small bows before the holy table. After this the deacon, bowing his head and pointing with the orarion to the Holy Bread, says in a quiet voice: "Bless, Master, the Holy Bread." And the priest, bowing, blesses the Holy Bread with the words: "And make this Bread." Deacon: "Amen." And again the deacon, pointing with the orarion to the holy chalice: "Bless, Master, the holy Cup." The priest blesses it with the words: "And that which is in this Cup." Deacon: "Amen." And once more the deacon, pointing with the orarion simultaneously to the diskos and the chalice, says: "Bless, Master, both." The priest blesses both, saying: "Changing them by Thy Holy Spirit." Deacon: "Amen, Amen, Amen." Bowing his head before the priest, the deacon returns to the previous place and, taking the fan, fans with it over the Holy Gifts. **136.** The priest recites quietly the prayer "That to those who shall partake" and, taking the censer, exclaims: "Especially for our most holy," thrice censes the Gifts from the front of the table. Then he covers the holy chalice with the small veil or purificator. The choir sings "It is truly meet" or, instead of "It is truly meet," the Heirmos of the feast that falls. During this singing, the deacon censes the holy table around and mentions whom he wishes of the deceased. And the priest quietly: "For the holy Prophet, Forerunner John" and mentions by name whom he wishes of the deceased: "And give them rest." After "It is truly meet" the priest exclaims: "Among the first, remember, O Lord." The deacon mentions the living. Choir: "And all mankind." The priest prays quietly: "Remember, O Lord, this city in which we live" and mentions by name whom he wishes of the living. Exclamation: "And grant us." Choir: "Amen." The priest turns to the west, however does not depart from the middle of the throne and blesses with the words "And may the mercies." Choir: "And with thy spirit." **137.** The deacon, having received the blessing from the priest, makes a small bow, goes around the holy table and goes out through the northern doors and, standing at his usual place, exclaims: "Having commemorated all the saints." The priest recites quietly the prayer "To Thee we entrust all our life." Exclamation: "And vouchsafe us, O Master." Choir: "Our Father." During the singing of the Lord's Prayer, the priest raises his hands, and after it exclaims: "For Thine is the kingdom." Choir: "Amen." The priest turns to the west, however does not depart from the middle of the holy table and blesses with the words "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Deacon: "Bow your heads unto the Lord." Choir: "To Thee, O Lord." The priest prays quietly: "We give thanks unto Thee." Exclamation: "Through the grace and compassions." Choir: "Amen." And immediately the priest reads quietly the prayer "Attend, O Lord," and the deacon, standing before the holy doors, girds himself with the orarion crosswise, if he did not do this at the prayer "Our Father." Then the priest and also the deacon, each at his place, make three small bows, saying quietly: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner," after which the priest uncovers the chalice. When the deacon sees that the priest has stretched out his hand to receive the Holy Bread, he exclaims: "Let us be attentive," and the priest, lifting the Holy Bread slightly up, exclaims: "Holy things to the holy." Choir: "One is Holy, One is Lord"; the Communion Hymn is sung. **138.** The deacon makes a small bow and enters through the southern doors into the sanctuary and, having stood to the right of the priest, makes once more a small bow and says: "Break, Master, the Holy Bread," and the priest breaks it attentively and piously into four parts in this manner: first he divides it into two parts and the part which he holds in the right hand, that is the one that has the inscriptions "XC" and "KA", he places on the diskos, then breaks across between the letters "IC" and "NI" the part which he holds in the left hand and places the particle "IC" at the top of the diskos, and the particle "NI" -- on the left; having taken then the second half, he breaks it in the middle between the letters "XC" and "KA" and places the particle "XC" at the bottom of the diskos, and the particle "KA" on the right edge of the diskos, so that the particles form the sign of the cross on the diskos. While doing this he says: "Broken and distributed." And the deacon, pointing with the orarion to the holy chalice, says: "Fill, Master, the holy Cup." The priest takes the upper particle, which has the sign "IC", makes with it the sign of the cross over the chalice and says: "The fullness of the Holy Spirit." And so he places it into the holy chalice. Deacon: "Amen." Then the priest wipes his fingers over the holy diskos. **139.** If there is the rite of the *zeon* [warm water], the deacon, presenting the warm water, says to the priest: "Bless, Master, the warm water," and the priest blesses it saying: "Blessed is the fervor of Thy saints." The deacon pours a little water in the sign of the cross into the holy chalice, saying: "The fervor of faith" and, having set aside the vessel with the warm water, stands slightly at a distance^[778]. **140.** The deacon goes around the holy table and, if necessary, washes the palm of his right hand and, at the words of the priest "Deacon, approach," approaches him from the left side, bows to him, asking forgiveness. The priest breaks the particle of the Holy Bread "XC" and gives a part of it to the deacon, and the deacon kisses his hand, takes the Holy Bread on the palm of his right hand, having placed it crosswise over the left and says: "Give unto me, Master." And the priest says: "To the sacred deacon (Name) is imparted." The deacon withdraws behind the throne, bowing his head, and prays like the priest with the words "I believe, O Lord, and I confess." Likewise the priest, having made a small bow, with two fingers of the right hand takes the second part of the particle "XC" and says: "The precious and most holy" and, bowing his head, prays with the words "I believe, O Lord, and I confess." And then they consume the Holy Bread from their hands with fear and all caution: first -- the priest, and then -- the deacon. **141.** Afterwards the priest, bowing down, takes the chalice in his right hand, and in his left a small purificator, holding it under his chin, and communicates of the Blood from the chalice, saying: "Of the precious and holy Blood of the Lord and God." And wipes his lips, as well as the edge of the holy chalice, with the small purificator, saying: "Lo, this has touched my lips." Then he calls the deacon with the words: "Deacon, approach." The deacon approaches and makes a small bow, saying: "Behold, I approach" and "Give unto me, Master." The priest takes the purificator and the chalice with his right hand, supporting the base of the chalice with his left. To the deacon, who holds the end of the purificator under his chin with both hands, the priest gives the holy chalice, saying: " The servant of God, deacon (Name), partakes." And after the communion of the deacon the priest says: "Lo, this has touched thy lips." The deacon, having lifted the holy diskos over the holy chalice, carefully wipes it with a sponge, if there is a custom to use it, so that not a single crumb remains on the diskos. Then, if there are no faithful for communion, he covers the holy chalice with the purificator and the small veil, and on the holy diskos places the folded star-cover and folded veils. And the holy doors are opened. **142.** The deacon makes a small bow, takes with piety the chalice from the priest and approaches the holy doors and, lifting the holy chalice, shows it to the people, saying: "With fear of God and with faith draw near." Choir: "Blessed is he that comes." The priest follows the deacon, takes from him the holy chalice and from the holy doors blesses the people with it: "O God, save," and both return to the holy table. If there be faithful for communion, the deacon, having placed the spoon into the chalice, covers it with the purificator or its veil, or both and, having made a small bow, receives it with piety from the priest, approaches the holy doors and, lifting the holy chalice, shows it to the people, saying: "With fear of God and with faith draw near." Choir: "Blessed is he that comes." The priest follows the deacon, takes from him the holy chalice and recites the prayer "I believe, O Lord." Simultaneously the deacon takes the diskos from the throne. After the completion of the prayer, the priest uncovers the holy chalice, holds the veil and purificator with his left hand and communicates with the spoon, saying "Of the precious, most holy." The deacon holds the diskos under the chin of the communicant. After communion the priest covers the chalice with the purificator or veil, or both, leaving the spoon in the chalice, blesses the people with it: "O God, save" and both return to the holy table. One may also do thus: the deacon covers the holy chalice with the purificator or its veil and, having made a small bow, receives piously the chalice from the priest, approaches the holy doors and, lifting the chalice, shows it to the people, saying: "With fear of God and with faith draw near." Choir: "Blessed is he that comes." The deacon returns to the holy table, where he places the chalice, from which he removes the small veil. The priest takes the holy chalice with the spoon and purificator, and the deacon -- the diskos and they go out of the sanctuary; those who wish to communicate approach. After the prayer "I believe, O Lord," which the priest leads, the faithful, with all piety and fear, having folded their arms crosswise on their chest, make a small bow and one by one approach for communion, or receive it in another manner, according to local custom. The priest, communicating, says to each communicant: "The precious, most holy." After the completion of the communion of the faithful, the priest leaves the spoon in the chalice and covers it with the purificator. Then, having returned with the deacon into the sanctuary, he places the Holy Gifts on the holy table, and the deacon covers the holy chalice with its veil. The priest takes once more the holy chalice and from the holy doors blesses the people with it, exclaiming: "O God, save Thy people." Choir: "We have seen the true light." And both return to the holy table. **143.** The priest places the holy chalice on the throne and censes it three times, praying quietly: "Be Thou exalted, O God, above the heavens." Then he gives the censer to the deacon and, having taken the holy diskos, places it on the deacon's head, and the deacon, holding it with piety in front and looking towards the holy doors, saying nothing, goes straight between the holy table and the holy doors to the table of oblation and places the holy diskos on it. After this he waits for the priest at the same place. And the priest, having made a small bow and taken the holy chalice, turned to the holy doors, looks at the people and says quietly: "Blessed is our God," and then exclaims: "Always, now and ever." Choir: "Amen. Let our mouths be filled." The priest goes to the table of oblation, after which the deacon censes the Holy Gifts and the priest. The priest, having placed the Holy Gifts and made a small bow, returns to the holy table. **144.** The deacon, having untied the orarion, as custom prescribes, goes out through the northern doors and, standing at the usual place, exclaims: "Arise! Having partaken of the divine." The priest recites quietly the Prayer of Thanksgiving "We thank Thee, O Master" and, having made with the Holy Gospel the sign of the cross over the folded antimension [*iliton*]^[779], places it on the antimension [*iliton*]. Exclamation: "For Thou art our sanctification." Choir: "Amen." The priest, going towards the holy doors, exclaims: "Let us depart in peace." Choir: "In the name of the Lord." Deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." The priest enters through the holy doors into the temple of the faithful and, standing between the two choirs (see no. 184), reads loudly the Prayer behind the Ambo^[780] "O Lord, Who blessest those who bless Thee." Choir: "Amen." And then: "Blessed be the name of the Lord" and, if there is a custom, Psalm 33(34) "I will bless the Lord." At the Prayer behind the Ambo, the deacon stands to the right and points with his orarion to the icon of the Savior. After the completion of the prayer, the priest enters the holy doors and, immediately returning to the table of oblation, recites the Prayer at the Consuming of the Holy Gifts "Thou who art the fulfillment of the Law." The deacon enters through the northern doors and consumes the Holy Gifts with fear and all caution. The priest, if there exists a custom, goes out through the holy doors and distributes the antidoron to the people, if not, the antidoron is distributed after the dismissal. **145.** After the completion of the psalm and the distribution of the antidoron, the priest stands in the holy doors and, blessing the people, exclaims: "The blessing of the Lord be upon you." Choir: "Amen." The priest, turned to the east, says: "Glory to Thee, O Christ God." Choir: "Glory, Both now," "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Bless." The priest turns again to the people, saying: "May Christ our true God." Choir: "Amen" (see no. 184).
