At solemn and extraordinary liturgies, the priest, turned to the people, exclaims the Polychronion, as custom prescribes. After this the priest enters the sanctuary and the holy doors are closed. At the end, the priest and deacon in the sanctuary or in the sacristy, take off the sacred vestments, saying: "Now lettest Thou" and wash their hands at the usual place. After the Small Dismissal they give thanks to God for everything and, having kissed the holy table, depart. **146.** In seminaries, houses of study and other places where there are many priests, the priest who serves as deacon performs his diaconal service fully, namely: he receives Holy Communion at that Liturgy at which he serves as deacon, from the hands of the priest, and consumes what remains after communion.
[^776]: The deacon stands to the left and together with the priest recites the dialogue, and then goes out through the northern doors, as is specified in no. 132.
[^777]: He does not make the sign of the cross with the *aer* nor kiss the throne.
[^778]: The rite of pouring warm water is not an absolute requirement (see no. 183). The Lviv Synod abolished it "for a significant reason" ("Appendix" 1897, § IV, p. 218).
[^779]: He holds the book vertically and thus makes the sign of the cross (see no. 119).
[^780]: This prayer is not read before the icon of the Savior, because it is -- "behind the ambo". Its content is directed to the "Father of Lights" (not to Christ), and the conclusion -- Trinitarian. **Chunk 77** **2. In Concelebration of Two Deacons** **147.** On solemn feasts two deacons serve the priest or concelebrants. **148.** At the appropriate time the priest enters the church and, together with both deacons, makes three small bows to the east before the holy doors. Then they do everything as at the Liturgy in concelebration with one deacon, and both respond to the priest. After the prayer "O Lord, stretch forth Thy hand" the priest, and with him the deacons, bow to the right and left choirs and depart into the sanctuary: the priest and the 1st deacon -- through the southern, and the 2nd deacon -- through the northern doors, saying "I will enter into Thy house." Having arrived in the sanctuary, they make three small bows before the holy table and kiss: the priest -- the Holy Gospel, and the deacons -- the holy table and all, if there exists a custom, -- the altar cross, which is on the holy table. Having vested, they wash their hands and prepare everything for the Proskomedia. Only the 1st deacon says: "Bless, Master" and everything else, and the Proskomedia is celebrated, according to custom. **149.** After the dismissal of the Proskomedia, the deacons cense the offering with three swings, and then go together with the priest before the holy table, saying quietly: "In the tomb with the body" and the rest, they cense together it from the front, then the 1st deacon -- the right side of the holy table, and the 2nd deacon -- the left, and again both together -- from the east, then -- the icon behind the altar and other icons of the sanctuary, as well as the 1st deacon -- the cross, and the 2nd deacon -- the icon of the Theotokos, if they be behind the throne (see no. 33). Then they go out of the sanctuary: the 1st deacon -- through the southern, and the 2nd -- through the northern doors. Having come before the holy doors, they cense the icons of the iconostasis: the 1st deacon begins from the icon of the Savior, and the 2nd -- from the icon of the Theotokos, after this the 1st deacon -- the right, and the 2nd -- the left choirs. They cense the faithful, one from the right, and the other from the left side whether from the solea, or, if there exists a custom, -- in the church itself, going to the very narthex, after which they enter the sanctuary: the 1st deacon -- through the southern, and the 2nd -- through the northern doors and cense once more the throne from the front with three swings and likewise the priest. **150.** Having given away the censers to the server, both approach the priest and do everything as at the Liturgy in concelebration with one deacon. They go out: the 1st deacon -- through the southern, and the 2nd -- through the northern doors and, having stood at their places before the holy doors, make three small bows, saying quietly thrice: "O Lord, open my lips." After this the 1st deacon begins: "Bless, Master." **151.** The first deacon sings the Great Litany. During the singing by the choir of the first Antiphon or Typika [Psalm], he makes a small bow, departs from his place and stands before the icon of Christ, holding the orarion with three fingers of his right hand, according to custom (see no. 120). After the completion of the Antiphon, the 2nd deacon, having approached and stood at the usual place, sings: "Again and again." When the choir sings the second Antiphon or Typika [Psalm], he does the same as the 1st deacon during the first Antiphon, and stands before the icon of the Theotokos. After the second Antiphon the choir sings: "Glory, Both now," "Only-begotten Son." The priest recites nothing quietly. Neither the priest nor the deacons bow their heads at "became man." Then the 1st deacon returns to his place and begins "Again and again." After the completion of the litany, both depart into the sanctuary: the 1st -- through the southern, and the 2nd -- through the northern doors and stand to the right and left of the priest. **152.** When the singers, who are singing the third Antiphon or the Beatitudes, reach "Glory" or the last verses of the Beatitudes, the priest and deacons make three small bows. Then the priest hands the Holy Gospel to the 1st deacon, and himself lowers the phelonion (see no. 34). The priest with the 1st deacon go around the holy table from the right side, during which the 2nd deacon takes the censer, and all go out through the northern doors, preceded by candle-bearers: first goes, censing, the 2nd deacon, then -- the 1st deacon, carrying the Holy Gospel, and behind them -- the priest. Having approached the holy doors, the candle-bearers stand on opposite sides: one -- near the icon of the Theotokos, and the other -- near the icon of the Savior, the 1st deacon -- on the right, and the 2nd -- on the left side, and the priest stands in the middle behind them. **

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

Diagram: At the Little Entrance** [Left Column] 6 ... 4 ... 2 [Center] D.2 ... D.1 ... Priest [Right Column] 5 ... 3 ... 1 The first deacon says: "Let us pray to the Lord," and the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Entrance. After the completion of the prayer the 1st deacon, pointing with his right hand to the east, says to the priest: "Bless, Master, the holy entrance." The priest blesses and the 1st deacon gives the priest the Holy Gospel for kissing. After the completion of the last verse of the Antiphon or Beatitudes, the 2nd deacon goes out to the center, and the 1st deacon, having stood behind him, exclaims: "Wisdom, arise." After this all enter the sanctuary, the 2nd deacon gives away the censer, and the 1st deacon places the Holy Gospel on the holy table^[781]. **153.** When the singers reach the last troparion, the 1st deacon says: "Bless, Master, the time of the Thrice-Holy," and the priest: "For Holy art Thou." The 1st deacon exclaims: "and unto ages of ages." During the singing of the Trisagion, both the priest and the deacons recite it. Then the priest goes with the deacons to the High Throne and says: "Blessed is he that comes," and the 1st deacon: "Bless, Master." **154.** After the completion of the Trisagion hymn, the deacons approach the holy doors and the 1st deacon says: "Let us be attentive." Priest: "Peace be to all," and the 2nd deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive!". After the Prokimenon the 1st deacon: "Wisdom" and, after the reading by the reader of the title of the Apostle, the 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive." At the end of the reading of the Apostle, the deacons with the priest return before the holy table. After the completion of the Apostle, the priest says: "Peace be to thee," and the 1st deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." **155.** During the singing of "Alleluia," the deacons, having taken censers and put in incense, approach the priest and say: "Bless, Master, the incense" and, having received the blessing, cense the holy table first from the front, then the 1st deacon -- from the right side, and the 2nd -- from the left and again both together -- from the east, then -- the icon behind the altar and other icons of the sanctuary, the 2nd deacon also -- the oblation, and both -- everything else, according to custom. Then the deacons, having placed the censers in their places, approach the priest and the 1st deacon exclaims: "Bless, Master, the proclaimer of the holy Apostle." Priest: "May God, through the prayers" and gives him the Gospel. The 2nd deacon: "Wisdom, arise, let us hear the Holy Gospel." Priest: "Peace be to all." The 1st deacon, having stood on the ambo or somewhat before the holy doors on the designated place: "The reading from the Holy Gospel according to (Name)." The 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive" and everything else, according to custom. **156.** Then the deacons go out through their doors and stand at the designated places, and the 1st deacon begins: "Let us all say." Then the 2nd deacon: "Pray, ye catechumens." 1st deacon: "All catechumens." 2nd deacon: "Catechumens, depart" and again the 1st deacon: "All catechumens, depart. Let no catechumen remain, only the faithful. Choir: "Lord, have mercy." 1st deacon: "Help us, save us, have mercy," "Wisdom." 2nd deacon: "Again and again," "Help us, save us, have mercy," "Wisdom." After this both enter the sanctuary. And the holy doors are opened^[782]. **157.** During the singing of the Cherubic Hymn, the deacons, having taken censers, put in incense and received the blessing, recite the 50th(51st) Psalm and cense the throne, the sanctuary and everything else, as was noted above concerning this (see no. 149). After the censing, the deacons stand on the sides of the priest, holding the censers on the ring finger of the left hand and together with the priest, lifting their hands up, recite all together three times the Cherubic Hymn, after each time making a small bow (see no. 129). Then, if there exists a custom, the priest kisses the holy table and the altar cross, and the deacons -- the edge of the holy table and, directly, in front -- the deacons, they go to the table of oblation. There the priest, having taken the censer from the 1st deacon, censes the Holy Gifts. The first deacon says to the priest: "Take up, Master." And the priest takes off the large veil and gives it to the 2nd deacon, who holds the censer on the ring finger of his right hand, and says: "Lift up your hands." Then the priest takes the holy diskos and places it on the head of the 1st deacon (see no. 129), and he holds the diskos with both hands in front, holding simultaneously with his left hand the end of the orarion. The priest himself takes the chalice. Then all, accompanied by candle-bearers, go out through the northern doors: the 2nd deacon, who goes out first, exclaims: "All of you, Orthodox Christians." After him the same is exclaimed by the 1st deacon, and the priest says: "Our most holy [Pontiff]." The deacons, having entered through the holy doors into the sanctuary, stand not far from them on opposite sides: the 2nd -- on the left, and the 1st -- on the right. After the words "All of you" the priest enters the sanctuary and, having approached the front with the deacons, places the holy chalice on the throne, also takes from the 1st deacon the holy diskos and places it on the throne to the left of the chalice; with the large veil, which he takes from the 2nd deacon and censes over the censer, he covers the Holy Gifts, then takes from the hands of the 2nd deacon the censer and censes with it the Holy Gifts (see no. 130). During this the holy doors are closed and the dialogue between the priest and both deacons takes place. Having given a bow to the priest, the deacons go out through their doors and stand at the usual place, and the 1st -- sings "Let us complete." **158.** The second deacon: "Let us love one another." The deacons, and simultaneously also the priest, make three small bows at their places and both deacons kiss each other on the left shoulder. The first deacon exclaims: "The doors, the doors." At "and became man" neither the deacons nor the priest bow their heads. First deacon: "Let us stand well." The deacons, having made a small bow, enter through their doors into the sanctuary and stand on the sides of the priest. The 1st deacon, if necessary, takes the fan or the small folded veil and fans over the Holy Gifts. At "Singing the triumphant hymn," the 2nd deacon takes with his right hand the star-cover and strikes with it on the holy diskos, as was said above about this and, having kissed it, lays it aside on the throne (see no. 133). **159.** During the exclamation of the words of consecration, the deacons together with the priest point with the orarion to the holy diskos, and then -- to the holy chalice. After the consecration of both the Holy Bread and the Holy Cup, the deacons bow low, making simultaneously the sign of the cross on themselves. After the words of the priest "Thine own of Thine own," which he says quietly, the 1st deacon takes in his right hand the holy diskos, and the 2nd deacon, also with the right hand, -- the holy chalice, so that the right hand of the 1st deacon rests on the right hand of the 2nd deacon. After this the deacons slightly lift the Holy [Gifts], tracing the sign of the cross over the antimension [*iliton*], and the priest exclaims: "Thine own of Thine own." Having placed the diskos and chalice, the priest and deacons make again a small bow. After this the priest recites quietly the prayer "Again we offer," during which the 1st deacon fans over the Holy Gifts, if necessary. After the completion of the prayer, the 1st deacon lays aside the fan or veil and both deacons approach the priest, who together with them makes three small bows. Then the 1st deacon, pointing with the orarion to the Holy Bread: "Bless, Master, the Holy Bread." After the blessing the deacons say: "Amen." Then the 1st deacon points with the orarion to the holy chalice: "Bless, Master, the holy Cup." To the blessing the deacons respond: "Amen." The first deacon points with the orarion to the Holy Gifts and says: "Bless, Master, both." The priest blesses both, saying: "Changing them by Thy Holy Spirit." Deacon: "Amen, Amen, Amen." Bowing their heads before the priest, both deacons return to the place where they stood before, and the 1st takes the fan and fans with it over the Holy Gifts, as noted above, if necessary. **160.** During the singing of "It is truly meet," the deacons cense the throne from the sides, each -- from his own, and from the east and commemorate the deceased, whom they wish. And after "Among the first, remember, O Lord," the deacons commemorate the living. After the exclamation "And grant that with one mouth," the deacons, having made a small bow, go out, with the permission of the priest, through their doors and stand at the usual place. The second deacon says: "Having commemorated all the saints." At the words of the priest "Peace be to all" and the response of the choir "And to thy spirit," the 2nd deacon exclaims: "Bow your heads unto the Lord." During the quiet prayer of the priest "We give thanks," the deacons stand before the holy doors and gird themselves with the oraria crosswise, if they did not do this earlier -- at "Our Father." After the priest opens the chalice, both he and the deacons, each at his place, make three small bows, saying quietly: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner." The first deacon exclaims: "Let us be attentive." The deacons enter through their doors into the sanctuary and, having stood on the sides of the priest, make a small bow, and the 1st says: "Break, Master, the Holy Bread." After the breaking of the Holy Bread, the 1st deacon says: "Fill, Master, the holy Cup." After the mixing of both kinds, at the time when warm water is to be poured, the same says: "Bless, Master, the warm water" and, pouring a little water, adds: "The fervor of faith." **161.** The priest invites the deacons to Holy Communion with the words: "Deacons, approach" and gives Holy Communion to the deacons, as prescribed. After the communion of the priest and deacons, the 1st deacon carefully wipes the diskos over the holy chalice and, if there are no faithful for communion, everything takes place as prescribed in the rubric of the Liturgy in concelebration with one deacon (see no. 142). If there are communicants, everything takes place as prescribed above, with the only difference that the priest before communion hands to the 2nd deacon the veil and purificator. **162.** After the censing, the priest gives the censer to the 2nd deacon, and places the holy diskos with the folded star-cover and folded veils on his head (see no. 129). The 2nd deacon, holding all this on his head and looking towards the doors and saying nothing, goes between the throne and the holy doors straight to the table of oblation, on which he places the diskos, and there awaits the priest. And the priest, having made a small bow and taken the holy chalice, departs, according to custom, to the table of oblation, after which the 2nd deacon censes the holy things and the priest, and after the prayer of the priest "Thou who art the fulfillment of the Law," with fear and all caution consumes the Holy Gifts remaining after Holy Communion, then unties his orarion. **163.** The first deacon, having untied, according to custom, the orarion, goes out through the northern doors and, standing at the designated place, says: "Arise! Having partaken." After the exclamation "For Thou art our sanctification," the priest: "Let us depart in peace." Choir: "In the name of the Lord." 1st deacon: "Let us pray to the Lord." Choir: "Lord, have mercy." During the Prayer behind the Ambo, the 1st deacon stands to the right, pointing with the orarion to the icon of the Savior, and after the prayer returns through the southern doors to the sanctuary. At the end, having made, according to custom, the dismissal, they take off all sacred vestments (see no. 145). **3. Without a Deacon** **164.** A priest who serves without a deacon performs and recites all that which belongs to the deacon, considering the following: **165.** He does not say "Bless, Master," "Let us pray to the Lord," "Take up, Master," etc., with the exception of what is said before the Prayer behind the Ambo, that is "Let us pray to the Lord." **166.** After the dismissal of the Proskomedia, the priest censes as the deacon: from the solea -- the iconostasis, both choirs and the people (see nos. 33 and 75). **167.** The prayers of the Great and Small Litanies the priest recites before the exclamation, and not after it. **168.** For the Little Entrance, the priest takes the Holy Gospel, goes around the throne from the right side and goes out through the northern doors. Bowing his head before the holy doors, he recites the Prayer of the Entrance "O Master, Lord our God," blesses the entrance with his right hand, kisses the Gospel and, showing it, exclaims: "Wisdom, arise." After this he enters the sanctuary through the holy doors (see no. 122, note). He finishes the Prayer of the Trisagion with the exclamation "For Holy art Thou," not turning to the people. After the Trisagion, he goes behind the throne, reciting the words of blessing, and sits on the southern side. **169.** When the choir finishes singing the Thrice-Holy Hymn, the priest exclaims: "Let us be attentive" and blesses: "Peace be to all. Wisdom, let us be attentive." The choir sings the Prokimenon. Priest: "Wisdom." The Reader announces the title of the Apostle. Priest: "Let us be attentive." After the reading of the Apostle he says to the reader: "Peace be to thee" and immediately after this: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." Choir: "Alleluia" with verses. Then the priest blesses the incense, takes the censer, censes the throne around, the whole sanctuary and from the solea -- the iconostasis, both choirs and the people. Already during this or even later he recites quietly the Prayer before the Gospel "Illumine our hearts." After the completion of "Alleluia" with verses, he exclaims: "Wisdom, arise, let us hear the Holy Gospel" and, blessing the people, says: "Peace be to all." Choir: "And to thy spirit." Priest: "The reading from the Holy Gospel according to (Name)." He takes after this the Book of the Gospels, places it on the analogion somewhat outside the holy doors and reads the Gospel, turned to the people. After the reading, he kisses the rolled book and places it on the middle of the throne or on its right side (see no. 126, note). **170.** Having recited the Prayer of the Cherubic Hymn, the priest blesses the incense, after which he then censes around the holy table, the icon behind the altar, the oblation and from the solea -- the iconostasis, both choirs and the people. Having returned to the throne and holding the censer on the ring finger of his left hand, he recites, having lifted his hands, three times the Cherubic Hymn. Then he approaches the oblation, with three swings censes the Holy Gifts, saying quietly: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner." Then he takes the large veil and places it on his own left shoulder, saying: "Lift up your hands," takes the holy diskos -- with the left, and the chalice -- with the right hand and goes out through the northern doors, exclaiming: "May the Lord God remember" (see no. 129). Having entered through the holy doors, he places the Holy Gifts on the throne, as is proper, censes the large veil over the censer, which the server presents, saying: "The noble Joseph." Then, having taken the censer from the hands of the server, he censes the Holy Gifts with three swings, saying: "Do good, O Lord." **171.** Having given away the censer, he exclaims the litany "Let us complete," "Help us, save us, have mercy." Reciting the Symbol of Faith he lifts the *aer* and holds it over the Holy Gifts. According to the prescription, exclaiming "Singing the triumphant hymn," he strikes the diskos with the star-cover as the deacon does, kisses it and lays it aside on the holy table (see no. 133). After the prayer "Remembering this," he crosses his hands: taking with the right hand the holy diskos, and with the left -- the holy chalice, and, lifting slightly, makes the sign of the cross over the antimension [*iliton*] and exclaims "Thine own of Thine own." After the exclamation "Especially for our most holy" he censes the holy table only from the front, and not around. Before the elevation of the Lamb he says: "Let us be attentive" and himself pours warm water into the chalice, according to the prescription. **172.** The priest, having gathered all particles that were on the diskos into the chalice, covers it with the purificator or veil, or even both, places the folded star-cover, small veil and *aer* on the diskos. Having drawn open the curtain of the iconostasis and opened the holy doors, he places the spoon on the chalice or puts it into the chalice and, having made a small bow, takes the holy chalice in his hands; approaches the holy doors and, showing the chalice, exclaims: "With fear." Immediately after this he recites: "I believe, O Lord, and I confess." After the completion of the prayers, he covers the chalice and administers communion with the spoon. Having finished the communion of the faithful, he leaves the spoon in the chalice, covers it with the purificator and veil and, blessing the people, exclaims: "O God, save Thy people." Having returned to the holy table, he places the chalice and censes it with three swings, saying: "Be Thou exalted." Having made a small bow, he takes with the right hand the holy chalice, and with the left -- the holy diskos, having said first quietly: "Blessed is our God," and then loudly: "Always, now and ever" and, turning to the people, goes to the table of oblation, on which he places everything. Having made after this a small bow, he returns to the holy table (see no. 142). **173.** One may also do thus: having communicated, the priest places the holy diskos on the holy chalice and covers it with the small veil or purificator, or even both. Having made a small bow, he takes the holy chalice and, showing it to the people, exclaims: "With fear." Having returned to the holy table, he takes the chalice and diskos between the index and middle fingers, takes the spoon with the right hand and begins to communicate the faithful. After the completion of communion, he leaves the spoon in the chalice, returns to the holy table and places the diskos and chalice on it, covers it with the small veil. After this he takes the chalice and, turning to the people, blesses them with the chalice, saying: "O God, save Thy people." Having placed the chalice on the holy table, he censes it with three swings, saying: "Be Thou exalted." Then he places the purificator under the small veil, with which the chalice is covered, and places the folded star-cover and the second small veil and *aer* on the holy diskos, makes a small bow, takes the holy chalice and, having turned to the holy doors, looking at the people, says quietly: "Blessed is our God"; after this exclaims: "Always, now and ever." Then he takes from the throne with his left hand the diskos and goes to the table of oblation, on which he leaves everything, and after a small bow returns to the holy table. **174.** The priest, exclaiming the thanksgiving litany "Arise! Having partaken," the prayer and the exclamation "For Thou art," folds the antimension [*iliton*] according to the prescription. After the dismissal he returns to the sanctuary and closes the holy doors. At the end he goes to the table of oblation and consumes there the Holy Gifts with fear and all caution, washes his hands and, having thanked God, departs. **4. Rubric of the Non-Solemn Divine Liturgy, that is, served ordinarily** **175.** All rites and ceremonies which we perform at the solemn Liturgy must be preserved also in the ordinary Liturgy, whether, as it is said, in the private Liturgy. What, according to the prescription, is to be exclaimed, let it be exclaimed so that it can be heard not only by the reader or singer, that is, the one who serves, but also by those present. **176.** The reader, if possible, should wear a sticharion. His usual place is outside the sanctuary. He stands directly on the right or on the left side of the iconostasis. If it is necessary to enter the sanctuary, for example, to give the priest the censer or warm water, he may enter only through the side doors. The priest closes and opens the holy doors, and draws the curtain shut and open himself. **177.** The use of the censer in Liturgies which we celebrate without any solemnity is not absolutely prescribed, but it will be very praiseworthy to use it. **178.** If there is a lack of time for reciting all the preparatory prayers before the iconostasis, let the priest never omit the prayer "O Lord, stretch forth Thy hand." Having entered the sanctuary, let him read the psalm "I will enter into Thy house" and, having kissed the holy table, the Gospel and, if there exists a custom, -- the altar cross, puts on the sacred vestments. **179.** The Proskomedia should be celebrated not in the sacristy, but on the side altar [table of oblation] which is located near the holy table. The custom of using five prosphora is not necessary, on the contrary, it is permitted to use only one prosphora at several liturgies, even if the sign of the Lamb on the prescribed side is not imprinted, however, at every Liturgy the priest is obliged to cut the bread and take out particles as if the bread were whole, not using dried lambs and not using either the Lamb or particles cut earlier by the one who serves. **180.** The Little Entrance with the Gospel is done according to the prescriptions, going around the holy table and going out of the sanctuary through the northern doors. **181.** After the Prayer of the Trisagion, the priest may omit the blessing of the High Throne. Turned to the west, he listens to the reading of the Apostle, having lowered the phelonion and hands under it. He may read the Gospel also without an analogion, when the server, if there exists a custom, supports the book with his head before the holy doors. **182.** The Great Entrance is done according to the prescriptions, going out through the northern doors. **183.** The priest does not fan over the Holy Gifts, unless there arises a danger that something might fall into the chalice. He does not pour warm water, if he cannot do this conveniently. **184.** He recites the Prayer behind the Ambo before the holy doors, and when he blesses and makes the dismissal, he stands in the very holy doors. **185.** After the dismissal he does not recite any other prayer, but immediately closes the holy doors. **5. With Concelebrants** **186.** Actual concelebrants are priests who, with the principal celebrant, exclaim the words of consecration, and non-actual, or ordinary assistants -- those who do not exclaim the words of consecration. Nothing prevents, if at a solemn concelebration, however not at an ordinary Liturgy, assisting priests join the actual concelebrants. **187.** Actual concelebrants, whether at a solemn Liturgy or at a private Liturgy, celebrate for the first accepted intention. **188.** Priests who actually concelebrate are obliged to recite all the priestly prayers as well as their endings, that is the exclamations, up to the very Prayer of Thanksgiving "We thank Thee" after communion inclusive. And the litanies each either exclaims himself, according to the prescribed order, or only listens, recites the prayers when the deacon or another priest exclaims the litany. Priests who only assist are not obliged to read the priestly prayers, for the principal celebrant is to recite them, but only to say the exclamations in turn. **189.** The rites and blessings are performed only by the principal celebrant himself. Bows are made by all together, they lift their hands where it is prescribed and can be done conveniently. **a) In the solemn form** **190.** It will be good if all together recite the introductory prayers before the iconostasis, but let only the principal priest kiss the icons. **191.** All concelebrants, while putting on the prescribed priestly vestments, recite the appropriate prayers. Then each, holding in his hands a small Liturgicon, stands at the side of the holy table or also behind it, however not before it, where only the principal celebrant with the deacons occupies the place, and so all arrange themselves, each according to the rank of his dignity or his ordination. The first among the concelebrants or those standing by stands on the right side of the principal celebrant, the second -- on the left, the third -- again on the right and so on. **192.** The Proskomedia is celebrated by one of the concelebrants and only he recites the Prayer of the Offering. However, all concelebrants may, according to their own intentions, place their particles (see no. 113). **193.** These exclamations belong to the principal celebrant: -- "For to Thee belongs," after the Great Litany; -- "For Holy art Thou," after the Prayer of the Trisagion; -- "For a merciful," after the litany "Let us all say"; -- "That being kept under Thy dominion always," after the Second Prayer of the Faithful; -- "Through the compassions," after the Prayer of the Offering; -- "Singing the triumphant hymn," before "Holy"; -- "Especially for our most holy," mentioning the Most Holy Theotokos; -- "And grant that with one mouth," at the end of the Anaphora; -- "And may the mercies," after the Anaphora; -- "And vouchsafe us, O Master," before "Our Father"; -- "For Thou art our sanctification," after communion. Other exclamations are taken by the concelebrants in turn. To better maintain order, the principal celebrant invites the concelebrants to exclaim with a nod of the head, and then the one who is to exclaim gives consent, bowing his head in the direction of the principal celebrant. **194.** For the Little Entrance all go out^[783], having lowered their hands under the lowered phelonion, through the northern doors, in front -- the younger ones, and stand before the holy doors in two rows, one near another, the principal celebrant stands with everyone in the middle. The principal celebrant himself recites the Prayer of the Entrance. After the call of the deacon: "Wisdom, arise" all enter behind the deacon through the holy doors into the sanctuary and occupy their places near the holy table. **

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

Diagram: Before the Little Entrance, before the Holy Doors** [Left Column] Candle-bearer ... 6 ... 4 ... 2 ... Concelebrants [Right Column] Candle-bearer ... 5 ... 3 ... 1 ... Concelebrants [Bottom] Celebrant ... Deacon **195.** The concelebrants sit near the High Throne in the same order in which they stand at the throne, that is, those who stand to the right of the principal celebrant sit to his right, and those on the left side -- sit to the right [sic - likely *left*]. **

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

Diagram: At the High Throne** [Left] 2 ... 4 ... 6 [Center] D (High Place) [Right] 1 ... 3 ... 5 **196.** During the reading of the Gospel all remain in their places, looking towards the ambo or the place from which the Gospel is read. **197.** At the Cherubic Hymn all lift their hands, if this can be done conveniently, but all recite the Cherubic Hymn and make the prescribed bows. During the censing of the holy table by the deacon all step away from it slightly so that the deacon can easily go around it. **198.** From the table of oblation each takes one of the things used in the Divine Sacrifice, namely: the spear, the spoon, holding them on their chests. All go out^[784] through the northern doors, in front -- the deacon, who exclaims: "All of you" and stands in the holy doors in the sanctuary, behind him other concelebrating priests, beginning from the youngest, exclaiming each: "All of you," one or even several, if there is a custom, and stand facing one another outside the sanctuary before the holy doors as at the Little Entrance. The principal priest exclaims: "Our most holy [Pontiff]" and stands exactly before the holy doors, turns to the west when he exclaims "All of you," after which he enters the sanctuary, and behind him go the concelebrants and each stands at the holy table at his place. **199.** Having made the Great Entrance, if there is no deacon, one of the concelebrants sings the first part of the litany "Let us complete," and another -- the second part, so that each has time to read the Prayer of the Offering. **200.** When the principal priest kisses the Holy Gifts, the concelebrants one by one approach the holy table, according to the order of their dignity. The principal priest, having stepped back slightly from the holy table, turns to the right side and looks to the north, and each concelebrant kisses first the Holy Gifts, and then the left and right shoulder of the principal priest and stands to his left, slightly behind. The second concelebrant kisses first the Holy Gifts, then -- the principal celebrant, and at the end -- the first concelebrant and stands on his right side. All others do likewise. The principal priest says: "Christ is in our midst," and the concelebrant responds: "He is and shall be." Likewise do also the others, who kiss one another. After the kiss of peace the celebrant returns before the holy table; the 1st concelebrant takes one edge of the *aer*, and the 2nd -- the second edge and fan with it over the Gifts. All others stand in their places and quietly recite the Symbol of Faith. **201.** The concelebrants offering the sacrifice point with their hand to the holy diskos, and then to the holy chalice, just as the principal celebrant, simultaneously, slowly and attentively, sing the words of consecration, recite together "Thine own of Thine own," but only the principal celebrant blesses the Gifts. The same applies also to the Epiclesis. One must ensure, especially in the Liturgy of St. Basil, that after the reading of the prayer which immediately precedes the consecration, all together with the serving priest exclaim from the beginning to the end the words of consecration. It will also be good if the principal celebrant pronounces the last words of this prayer louder so that the concelebrants can hear them, and watches that all are ready already for the simultaneous exclamation of the words of consecration (see no. 134). **202.** The first part of the litany "Having commemorated all the saints" is sung by one of the concelebrants, if there is no deacon, and the second part -- by another, so that all have time to read the prayer "To Thee we entrust all our life." **203.** After the breaking [of the Lamb], the principal celebrant calls the deacon and gives him a particle of the Holy Bread, as prescribed. Then all recite the prayer "I believe, O Lord" and the principal priest communicates of the Body of Christ. All concelebrants, in turn, according to their dignity, approach the holy table from the side of the oblation table, and the principal celebrant stands on the opposite side of it. After the communion of the Body of Christ, each goes to the north of the holy table and washes, if necessary, his fingers in the vessel standing on the table of oblation, and, according to the prescribed sequence, they go behind the 1st concelebrant, who stands at his place at the holy table. The deacon consumes the particle of Bread after the priests. The principal celebrant, having returned to the center, communicates of the Most Precious Blood and moves away from the holy table; after this the concelebrants, according to the prescribed order, approach the holy table, this time from the southern side, and each after the communion of the Blood departs by the table of oblation and stands at his place at the holy table. At the end the deacon receives, according to the prescription, the communion of the Most Precious Blood from the principal celebrant. 

[INSERT DIAGRAM/TABLE HERE FROM ORIGINAL PDF]

[Diagram: Communion of the Body / Communion of the Blood] [Table of Oblation] 4 3 | 4 3 2 1 | 2 1 [Holy Table] [Principal Celebrant] [Principal Celebrant] **204.** Each, having just communicated, wipes his lips with the purificator at the edge of the chalice. **205.** The Prayer behind the Ambo is exclaimed, standing between the two choirs, by the principal celebrant. Only after the dismissal and after the holy doors are closed does each take off the sacred vestments. **6) In the Ordinary, or Private Form** **206.** There is no non-actual celebrant, or assistant, at the ordinary or private service. **207.** Everything that was said about concelebration in the solemn form is valid also for concelebration in the ordinary or private form, with the following exceptions: **208.** In seminaries and houses of religious education it will be good if the deacon participates in the celebration of the Divine Liturgy also when serving with the simple rite and if ordinary singing is used. Here, however, it is recommended to observe the rules which are binding for simple concelebration without a deacon. **209.** If there is no time for the recitation of the preparatory prayers before the iconostasis, which all concelebrants recite together or each separately, it is never permitted to omit the prayer "O Lord, stretch forth Thy hand." Having entered the sanctuary, they recite the psalm "I will enter into Thy house" and, having kissed the holy table, the Gospel and, if there exists a custom, -- the altar cross, they put on the priestly vestments (see no. 178). **210.** The members of the litanies are distributed among the concelebrants and are sung so that the one who does not sing the litanies has time to recite the corresponding prayer without haste. If there be two concelebrants, they sing the liturgical litanies alternately, having recited first quietly the corresponding prayer of each litany, but the prayer of the Great Litany and the Prayer of Thanksgiving after communion they recite quietly after the litany, but before the exclamation. It should also be noted that the first part of the litany after the Great Entrance and the litanies after the Anaphora are said by the second priest, who after that recites quietly the prayer; and the second part with the exclamation is recited by the first. If there be three concelebrants, then the 1st says the Great Litany, the 2nd -- the first Small Litany, the 3rd -- the second Small Litany; the 1st -- again the Litany after the Gospel; the 2nd -- the Litany of the Catechumens; the 3rd -- the first Small Litany of the Faithful, and the 1st -- the second; the 2nd -- the first part of the litany after the Entrance and after the Anaphora, and the 3rd -- the second part of those litanies; at the end the 1st -- the Thanksgiving Litany after communion. Such a method of distribution of various litanies among individual concelebrants is not prescribed absolutely, but only recommended to be used for greater convenience. **211.** It is not required that all concelebrants go out for the Little Entrance, but if they go out, then the one who is the 1st among them carries the Gospel, he himself recites the Prayer of the Entrance and imparts the blessing. But it is always required that those standing before the holy table or on its right side, before they go out, go around the holy table and go out behind the holy doors. **212.** There will be no blessing of the High Throne and all must remain near the throne during the reading of the Apostle. **213.** For the Great Entrance not all have to go out. If only the 1st makes the Entrance, he himself places the *aer* on his left shoulder and himself exclaims: "Our most holy [Pontiff]." If all go out, then each does not have to take some object used for the Divine Sacrifice, only the 2nd concelebrant takes the holy diskos, which he holds on his head, and the 1st -- the holy chalice; the 2nd exclaims: "All of you, Orthodox Christians," and the 1st: "Our most holy [Pontiff]." Others exclaim nothing (see no. 200). **215.** Everything else that the deacon is supposed to say or do, according to what was said about the celebration of the Liturgy without a deacon (comp. nos. 164-174), the concelebrant says and does. The one who serves the Proskomedia also cleanses the holy vessels after communion.
[^781]: Here neither the deacon nor the priest (when serving alone) makes the sign of the cross with the book of the Holy Gospel, but only lifts it up (a sign for attention).
[^782]: In the shortened form this part is not taken. Deacon exclaims: "Only the faithful, again and again in peace let us pray to the Lord".
[^783]: No participation of all in the exit is required (see nos. 211 and 213).
[^784]: Form of current diskoses does not allow to fulfill this requirement, therefore the deacon holds the diskos in his hands. **Chunk 78** **VI. Rubric of the Liturgy of Presanctified Gifts** **216.** On the Holy and Great Forty Days [Lent] at the Proskomedia of the Divine Liturgy on Sunday or on the last day before the Liturgy of Presanctified Gifts, besides the Lamb that is to be consecrated on that day, other Lambs are also prepared for those Liturgies of Presanctified Gifts that are to be celebrated on the following days. Having cut, sacrificed and pierced the first Lamb, the priest performs the same rites also over the other Lambs, reciting at each of them: "In remembrance," "As a sheep," "Sacrificed," "One of the soldiers" and places them one near another on the diskos. Then he pours wine and water into the holy chalice, having recited what is prescribed and, according to custom, finishes the Proskomedia. **217.** When the Lamb is to be blessed at the invocation of the Holy Spirit, he says: "And make this Bread" in the singular, and not in the plural, for Christ is -- only one. **218.** At the elevation he elevates simultaneously all consecrated Lambs; breaks only the first Lamb, places a part into the holy chalice and pours warm water when prescribed. After this he takes the other holy Lambs and places them in the pyx in the tabernacle. **219.** Then, according to custom, the priest recites the prayers, communicates and finishes the sacrifice according to the prescription. **1. In Concelebration of One Deacon** **220.** For the reading of the Hours, the priest in the epitrachelion stands before the holy doors and begins: "Blessed is our God." Reader: "Amen," "O Heavenly King" and the rest. After "Our Father" the priest, having said the exclamation, enters the sanctuary through the southern doors. The 3rd, 6th, 9th Hours are read, as well as the Typika. **221.** At the end of the Typika the priest and deacon vest in the sacred vestments as usual, but putting on each [vestment] they say nothing more, but only "Let us pray to the Lord." **222.** When the reader finishes the Typika, having recited the Trisagion, "Our Father," "Lord, have mercy" (12) and the prayer "Most Holy Trinity," the holy doors are opened. Priest: "Wisdom." Choir: "More honorable than the Cherubim." Priest: "Glory to Thee, O Christ God." Choir: "Glory, Both now," "Lord, have mercy" (3), "Bless." The priest makes the dismissal with the commemoration of the holy temple and the holy day. After this the holy doors are closed again. **223.** The priest accompanied by the deacon makes three small bows before the holy table and recites only: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner." They kiss, as was already noted, the Holy Gospel, the holy table and the altar cross. Then the deacon, having received permission from the priest, goes out through the northern doors and, having stood at the usual place, makes three small bows, saying nothing and says: "Bless, Master." The priest, standing before the holy table and making with the Holy Gospel the sign of the cross over it, exclaims: "Blessed is the kingdom." Choir: "Amen." Immediately the Reader: "Come, let us worship" (3) and reads the opening psalm (see nos. 102, 118, 119, note). **224.** The deacon returns into the sanctuary through the southern doors, and the priest, having stood before the holy doors, reads the Vespers (Lamp-lighting) Prayers from the fourth to the eighth, for the first three he will read later, at the Antiphons. **225.** At the end of the opening psalm the priest returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary, and the deacon, having gone out through the northern and stood at the usual place, sings the Great Litany. After the exclamation, having made a small bow, he returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary. The Reader begins the 18th Kathisma of the Psalter. At "Alleluia" -- they make small bows. When at each of the following Antiphons "Glory" is said, the deacon goes out through the northern doors from the sanctuary and at the designated place sings the Small Litany, and the priest recites quietly the first, second and third Vespers Prayers. After the completion of the Small Litany the deacon returns through the southern doors into the sanctuary, and the priest says the exclamation, as prescribed. **226.** At the beginning of the reading of the psalms [stichologia], if the Presanctified Lamb is kept in the tabernacle (artophorion) of the holy table, the transfer to the table of oblation takes place thus^[785]: the deacon brings to the holy table the holy diskos, the star-cover and the small veil. The priest kisses the Holy Gospel and places it on the right side of the holy table. After this he places the diskos on the unfolded antimension [*iliton*], on its left side, and, having opened the tabernacle, makes a small bow. He takes the chalice with the lid, in which the Lamb is kept, places it on the middle of the antimension [*iliton*] and, having taken from it the Presanctified Bread, places it with great piety on the holy diskos, as also the particles needed for the communion of the faithful. Having placed the pyx back into the tabernacle, he closes it and, having placed the holy diskos on the middle of the antimension [*iliton*], censes the star-cover and the small veil and covers the diskos with it. Having taken the censer, he censes around the holy table, preceded by the deacon with a lighted candle. Having returned before the holy table and given the censer to the deacon, he makes a low (prostrate) bow, making the sign of the cross on himself, after which he takes with both hands the covered holy diskos and, holding it on his head (see no. 129, note) crosses by the right side of the holy table to the table of oblation (altar of preparation), preceded by the deacon with a lighted candle and censer. **227.** At the table of oblation the priest places the diskos on the unfolded antimension [*iliton*], after which he pours wine and water into the chalice, as is the custom, saying nothing at this. After censing the veil of the chalice over the censer he covers the chalice with it. Then with the large veil, which he likewise censes, he covers the diskos and chalice, saying nothing at this, but only: "Through the prayers of our holy fathers, Lord Jesus Christ our God, have mercy on us." Having made a prostrate bow, the priest and deacon return to the holy table. There the priest places the Book of the Holy Gospels on the folded antimension [*iliton*]. **228.** If the Presanctified Lamb is kept in the tabernacle which is located on the table of oblation, then at the beginning of the reading of the psalms [stichologia] the priest and deacon go to the table of oblation. Both make a small bow before it, the priest opens the tabernacle and, having made again a small bow, censes with three swings the Presanctified Gifts. Then he takes the Presanctified Bread from the pyx and places it with great piety on the diskos, and pours into the holy chalice, according to custom, wine and water, saying nothing. He takes the censer, censes the star-cover and veils, covers the diskos and chalice, each -- with its own veil and both -- with the large veil (aer), saying nothing, but only: "Through the prayers of the holy fathers." Having made a prostrate bow, he returns to the holy table. **229.** If the priest deems it appropriate, he finishes the rite of placing the Lamb on the diskos during the reading of the first Antiphon, the censing -- during the second, and the transfer of the Presanctified Gifts -- during the reading of the third Antiphon. **230.** If a larger number of faithful is expected for communion, so that the Presanctified Bread alone will not suffice, the priest places the appropriate number of already consecrated particles on the diskos, and on top of them -- the Lamb Itself (see no. 114). **231.** After the completion of the reading of the psalms [stichologia] the choir begins the psalm "Lord, I have cried," and the deacon censes according to the prescription (see no. 33), at this he censes the Presanctified Gifts -- three times, each time -- with three swings. **232.** During the singing of "Glory, Both now" the holy doors are opened and the Entrance takes place in the usual manner. The deacon censes, if there be an Entrance with the Gospel, and makes the Entrance with the Gospel. **233.** When the deacon says in a low voice: "Let us pray to the Lord," the priest recites quietly the Prayer of the Entrance with its exclamation and, after the completion of the stichera, the deacon exclaims: "Wisdom, arise." Choir: "O Gladsome Light." They enter the sanctuary, then the deacon, turned to the holy doors, says: "Let us be attentive." The priest, having turned to the people, blesses: "Peace be to all." Deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." The choir sings the Prokimenon of the first Paremia. Deacon: "Wisdom." Reader, having stood in the middle between the two choirs and looking to the east: "The reading from the Book of Genesis." Deacon: "Let us be attentive." The Reader reads the first Paremia. After this the choir sings the second Prokimenon. **234.** Immediately after the second Prokimenon the deacon says to the priest: "Command," and the priest takes with both hands the lighted candle and simultaneously the censer, stands before the holy table, looking to the east and, making the sign of the cross, exclaims: "Wisdom, arise." After this he turns to the west, towards the people, makes again the sign of the cross and says in a raised voice: "The Light of Christ illumines all." At these words all who are in the sanctuary and in the church make three great prostrations. The priest turns again to the east and gives the candle and censer to the server. Reader: "The reading from the Book of Proverbs." Deacon: "Let us be attentive." The holy doors are closed and the second Paremia is read. **235.** After the completion of the second Paremia the priest says to the reader: "Peace be to thee," and the deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." After this the deacon, having taken a lighted candle, approaches the priest. The Reader, who stands in the middle between the two choirs, or rather the priest, who stands in the sanctuary before the holy table and censes, sings: "Let my prayer be set forth." After the singing of this verse by the reader or priest, the choir sings it once more. Then again the reader or priest, who now, accompanied by the deacon going in front, stands on the southern side of the holy table and censes there, sings the first verse of the 140th Psalm: "Lord, I have cried," and the choir repeats: "Let my prayer be set forth." And again the reader or priest, accompanied by the deacon, stands at the east of the holy table, censes there and sings the second verse of the psalm: "Set, O Lord, a watch before my mouth," and the choir sings: "Let my prayer be set forth." After this the reader or priest, preceded by the deacon, stands on the northern side of the holy table, censes there and sings the third verse of the psalm: "Incline not my heart," and the choir sings: "Let my prayer be set forth." And once more the reader or priest accompanied by the deacon, again stands before the throne, censes there and sings: "Let my prayer be set forth as incense before Thee," and the choir finishes: "the lifting up of my hands as an evening sacrifice." **236.** It should be noted that during the singing by the reader or priest of "Let my prayer be set forth" or the verse, the priest censes the holy table with three swings at the beginning and at the end of each verse which he sings. At this time the choir and the faithful pray on their knees. When the choir sings the priest, having given the censer to the server, and all who are in the sanctuary, pray likewise on their knees. After the completion all bow three times. **237.** If on these days of Lent falls the memory of a certain saint or a temple feast, having opened the holy doors, the deacon exclaims: "Let us be attentive," and the reader reads the Prokimenon of the Apostle, after which the Apostle and Gospel are read, as prescribed. **238.** The holy doors are closed and the deacon, having received permission from the priest, goes out through the northern doors and, having stood at the designated place, sings the litany "Let us all say." Everything else takes place according to the prescription until the very exclamation of the prayer for the catechumens, after which the priest, having laid aside the Gospel, unfolds the antimension [*iliton*] on the holy table. **239.** From Wednesday of the fourth week of Great Lent, which is the midpoint of the Forty Days, after the exclamation "That with us they also," the deacon dismisses the catechumens, and having invited to prayer those preparing for holy baptism: "All catechumens, depart. Catechumens, depart. All who are for illumination, approach" and so it is sung at all services of the Presanctified, even if a feast day fell, with the exception of Saturday and Sunday. After this follow the prayers of the faithful, according to the prescription. **240.** After the exclamation "According to the gift of Thy Christ" Choir: "Amen" and sings the hymn "Now the Powers of Heaven." The deacon, having returned through the northern doors into the sanctuary, opens the holy doors and, having taken the censer, censes with three swings only the front of the throne, then -- the table of oblation and the priest. Then he stands before the throne to the right of the priest and holds the censer on the ring finger of his left hand. The priest and deacon, with hands raised up, recite together "Now the Powers of Heaven" three times, each time making a small bow. **241.** Then they go directly to the table of oblation. There the priest, having taken the censer, censes with three swings the Presanctified Gifts, saying nothing at this, takes the large veil (aer) and places it on the left shoulder of the deacon, then takes the covered holy diskos with his right hand and holds it on his head, and the chalice with wine -- with his left hand at his chest (see no. 129, note). **242.** If, however, the diskos should not have a foot, the priest places it on the covered chalice, which he holds with his left hand, and with his right hand holds the veil over the holy diskos and carries the chalice like a diskos to his forehead. **243.** They go out of the sanctuary through the northern doors, in front walks the deacon, who frequently censes the Holy Gifts. During the procession no one says anything. When they enter through the holy doors into the sanctuary, the priest places the holy diskos on the throne on the left, and the holy chalice -- on the right side, removes the small veils from the diskos and chalice and places them on the holy table, and with the *aer*, which he takes from the shoulder of the deacon and censes over the censer, covers the Holy Gifts, saying nothing, but only censing the Holy Gifts thrice. After the completion of the hymn "Now the Powers of Heaven" all make three great prostrations, after which the holy doors are closed and the curtain is drawn shut. **244.** The deacon, having bowed to the priest, goes out through the northern doors and, having stood at the usual place, exclaims: "Let us complete," "Help us, save us, have mercy." The priest exclaims: "And vouchsafe us, O Master," and the people: "Our Father." The deacon girds himself with the orarion crosswise, as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom. **245.** According to the prescription follows the bowing of heads, and after the prayer "Look down, O Lord Jesus Christ" the priest and deacon make three small bows, after which the priest does not uncover the Holy Gifts, but, placing his right hand under the *aer*, touches the Life-giving Bread piously and with fear, and at the words of the deacon "Let us be attentive" exclaims: "The Presanctified Holy Things to the holy." Then the priest removes the *aer* and, having folded it, places it aside, as also the star-cover. The deacon enters through the southern doors into the sanctuary, stands to the right of the priest and, having made a small bow, says: "Break, Master, the Holy Bread," and the priest breaks it and places the four parts on the diskos just as it takes place at the Liturgy of Chrysostom, and the particle with the inscription "IC" he places into the holy chalice, saying nothing. The deacon pours a little warm water into the chalice, if there exists a custom, saying nothing and stands somewhat to the side. The choir sings the Communion Hymn "Taste and see," and also a second one, if the Apostle and Gospel of some saint or temple saint were read. **246.** The priest and deacon communicate according to custom of the Holy Bread. Then the priest wipes his fingers with a sponge, if there is a custom to use it, and, having kissed it, places it on its place. The deacon wipes the holy chalice, saying nothing and, having made three small bows, after the curtain of the iconostasis has been drawn open, opens the holy doors. Having received the chalice from the priest, he approaches the holy doors and, lifting it, shows it to the people, saying: "Draw near." Choir: "I will bless the Lord at all times. Alleluia." The communion of the faithful takes place just as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom, and the priest, giving the Holy Bread, says the words of this Liturgy "The precious and most holy." The transfer of the holy diskos takes place just as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom. The priest makes a small bow, takes the holy chalice, turns to the holy doors, looking at the people, says quietly: "Blessed is God," and then exclaims: "Always, now and ever." **247.** Everything else takes place just as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom. However, it should be noted that: 1) at the dismissal of this Liturgy the author is not mentioned; 2) in the three first days of Passion Week one must say the dismissal of Palm Sunday at Vespers: "Christ, our true God, Who came to His voluntary Passion." After the completion of the Liturgy of Presanctified Gifts the priest and deacon take off the holy vestments, saying nothing. **2. In Concelebration of Two Deacons** **248.** After the completion of the Hours and after the dismissal at the end of the Typika the holy doors are closed, the priest and deacons make before the holy table three small bows each, saying: "O God, be merciful to me a sinner" and kiss the Holy Gospel, the edge of the holy table and the altar cross, as usual. After this the 1st deacon, having paid respect to the priest, goes out through the northern doors and, having stood at his place before the holy doors, makes three small bows, saying nothing, after which he exclaims: "Bless, Master." Priest: "Blessed is the kingdom." Choir: "Amen" and the reader reads the opening psalm. The priest, having gone out through the northern doors, reads the Vespers Prayers, from the fourth to the eighth. At the end of the opening psalm the 1st deacon goes out through the northern doors and sings the Great Litany. After the exclamation "For to Thee belongs" the deacon returns into the sanctuary. **249.** The first deacon assists the priest during the placing of the Presanctified Lamb on the diskos and its transfer to the table of oblation, and the 2nd deacon goes out through the northern doors and sings the first Small Litany. The 1st deacon sings -- the second and finally the 2nd deacon -- the third. **250.** The censing on the psalm "Lord, I have cried" and the entrance take place just as at Vespers in concelebration with two deacons (see no. 39). Having returned into the sanctuary, the 1st deacon exclaims from the holy doors: "Let us be attentive." The priest, turned to the people: "Peace be to all." 2nd deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." The choir sings the Prokimenon of the first Paremia. 1st deacon: "Wisdom." Reader: "The reading from the Book of Genesis." 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive." The Reader reads the first Paremia, after which the choir sings the second Prokimenon. **251.** After the second Prokimenon the 1st deacon, turning to the priest, says: "Command." The priest takes the candle and censer and makes the sign of the holy cross, as was said above. Reader: "The reading from the Book of Proverbs." 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive." **252.** After the second reading of the Old Testament both deacons go before the priest when he censes the holy table and sings: "Let my prayer be set forth" with the verses of the 140th Psalm. **253.** If the memory of some saint or a temple feast falls, the 2nd deacon exclaims: "Let us be attentive." After the Prokimenon of the Apostle the 1st deacon: "Wisdom." After the reading by the reader of the title of the Apostle the 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive." After the completion of the reading of the Apostle the priest says: "Peace be to thee." 1st deacon: "Wisdom, let us be attentive." Choir sings "Alleluia". The censing before the Gospel takes place just as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom in concelebration of two deacons (see no. 155). Then the 1st deacon: "Bless, Master, the proclaimer." Priest: "May God, through the prayers" and gives him the Gospel. 2nd deacon: "Wisdom, arise, let us hear the Holy Gospel." Priest: "Peace be to all." 1st deacon, having stood on the ambo or somewhat before the holy doors: "The reading from the Holy Gospel according to (Name)." 2nd deacon: "Let us be attentive" and everything else, as is customary. **254.** After the reading of the Gospel the deacons, having gone out through their doors, stand at the designated places. 1st deacon begins: "Let us all say." Then 2nd deacon: "Pray, ye catechumens." 1st deacon: "All catechumens." 2nd deacon: "Catechumens, depart" and again 1st deacon: "Only the faithful." From the Wednesday of the fourth week of Lent they sing thus, as is given further. 1st deacon: "All catechumens." 2nd deacon: "Catechumens, depart." Again 1st deacon: "All who are for illumination, approach. Pray, ye who are for illumination." Choir: "Lord, have mercy," and the 1st deacon: "Ye faithful, for the brethren who are preparing for holy illumination." Priest -- exclamation: "For Thou art our enlightenment." 1st deacon: "All who are for illumination, depart." Again 1st deacon: "Only the faithful." Then 1st deacon: "Help us, save us, have mercy," "Wisdom." 2nd deacon: "Again and again," "Help us, save us, have mercy," "Wisdom." The deacons enter through their doors into the sanctuary. **255.** During the singing of the hymn "Now the Powers of Heaven" the holy doors are opened and the deacons, having taken censers, cense with three swings (thrice) only the front of the holy table, then -- the table of oblation and the priest. After this they stand to the right and left of the priest, holding the censers on one of the fingers of the left hand, and recite with the priest three times the hymn "Now the Powers of Heaven." Then they go straight to the table of oblation. There the priest censes the Presanctified [Gifts] and, having taken the *aer*, places it on the left shoulder of the 1st deacon, and all go out in the usual manner. In front go both deacons and frequently cense the Holy Gifts. **256.** After the holy diskos and the holy chalice are placed on the holy table, the deacons go out through their doors and stand at the usual places. 1st deacon exclaims: "Let us complete." At "Our Father" the deacons gird themselves with the oraria crosswise. 2nd deacon: "Bow our heads unto the Lord." After three small bows the 1st deacon exclaims "Let us be attentive" and after the exclamation of the priest "The Presanctified Holy Things to the holy" both deacons return through their doors into the sanctuary. 1st deacon: "Break, Master, the Holy Bread." The deacons communicate of the Holy Bread, according to custom. After the communion of the priest and deacons, the 1st deacon wipes the holy diskos over the holy chalice and calls: "Draw near." The rest takes place just as at the Liturgy of Chrysostom. **3. Without a Deacon** **257.** If this Liturgy is celebrated without a deacon, the priest exclaims everything that belongs to the deacon, as has already been said in the rubric of Vespers and the Divine Liturgy of John Chrysostom. **258.** When the priest censes the holy table and transfers the Holy Gifts to the table of oblation, the server, holding a lighted candle, walks before him. Small litanies and exclamations the priest says, if possible, before the holy table. **259.** During the singing of "Let my prayer be set forth" the server walks with a lighted candle before the priest. **260.** At the Great Entrance candle-bearers, if there be such, turned to the northern doors and arranged in order, accompany the Presanctified Lamb. After they arrive before the holy doors they stand together on both sides, and then return to their places. **4. In Concelebration of Priests** **261.** The rules of concelebration of the Liturgy of Presanctified Gifts -- are the same as of Vespers and the Liturgy of Chrysostom. Only one must keep in mind that: -- At the end of the Typika concelebrants vest in sacred vestments, saying when putting on each only: "Let us pray to the Lord." -- The principal celebrant exclaims: "For to Thee belongs," "For a merciful," "According to the gift of Thy Christ," "For Thou art our sanctification." Other exclamations are exclaimed by concelebrants in turn. -- At "Let my prayer be set forth" concelebrants remain in their places, stepping back slightly from the holy table when the principal celebrant needs to pass, together with the principal [celebrant] they bend their knees and rise. -- At the Great Entrance the celebrants carry nothing, however the 1st concelebrant may carry the chalice before the principal celebrant.
[^785]: I corrected it (Dutka Ivan), because here it was written "does not happen", but this is an incorrect translation.
